# KENJI — BOOK FOUR: *The Ronin*
## *Fraying Empire*

**Single manuscript — Book 4 (*Fraying Empire*):** The Ronin arc (Greymere → Greenveil → Thornfield → Millhaven → east road / Ashenveil border). Per-chapter source of truth: `Book 4/Chapters/` (`fraying_empire_chapter_01.md` … `fraying_empire_chapter_42.md`). Rebuild with `Book 4/build_story_book4_manuscript.py` after chapter edits. **Campaign bible (DM):** `fraying_empire_campaign.md` (*The Fraying Crown*).

---

*The Wizard King stepped away. The kingdom still runs on habit and competent people who are running out of duct tape. Kenji is somewhere smaller — a name he is not using, a village that needed a wall — until the world remembers where to knock.*

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter One: *Greymere*

### Day 229 — Morning — The Hearthstead, Greymere Valley

---

The fog hasn't burned off yet. The valley smells like wet grass and woodsmoke. I step off the porch barefoot, two training swords from the barn rack — oak, weighted to match Emberfrost's balance. The linen shirt sticks to my shoulders in the damp.

Haste clicks into place. The world slows. The fog droplets hang. The creek at the bottom of the hill sounds like it's moving through honey.

Enhanced Arcane Edge hums through the wood. Force energy sheaths both blades — faint gold shimmer along the grain. Training swords that hit like enchanted steel.

The bear is where it always is. Forty yards south, at the blackberry thicket on the property line. Brown. Old. Fat from six months of nobody bothering it. It's been eating my blackberries since I moved in.

I walk toward it. Stance loose. The new form: thumb on the guard, left foot forward, weight low. Past the cross-guard, past the dual-wield. The iaido stance I've been carving into muscle memory for six months. Draw, strike, return. One motion. One breath.

The bear looks up. Berry juice on its muzzle. It huffs. Stands. Nine feet tall on its hind legs. Paws the size of dinner plates.

Just like the forest outside Duskfen. Day Two. Rocks and borrowed armor and no idea what I was doing.

Two hundred and twenty-seven days later, I know exactly what I'm doing.

The bear charges.

---

Do. The nodachi draws low across the belly in a single arc — red-black steel trailing gold force energy. The abyssal edge passes through fur and muscle and rib like they're fog. The bear doesn't make a sound. It doesn't have time.

Men. The blade rises without pause. Same breath. Same draw. The return arc catches the falling skull from crown to jaw. The abyssal edge hums — red-black light flaring once along the cutting plane.

The bear's head doesn't hit the ground. It comes apart in a wash of dark red particulate — ash and light and nothing. The body follows a half-second later. Dissolving from the neck down. Red-black motes rising into the morning fog like embers from a dead fire.

Nothing left. No blood. No carcass. Just blackberry bushes and trampled grass and the faint smell of ozone.

Five steps back. Measured. The hakama whispers against the wet grass.

Chiburi. One sharp flick — the blade snaps right, parallel to the ground. Nothing to clean. The abyssal edge doesn't hold blood. It holds nothing. What it cuts, it unmakes.

Noto. The blade returns to the scabbard. One motion. The click of the guard seating.

The fog is burning off. The blackberry thicket is empty. Somewhere in the valley, a bird that stopped singing starts again.

---

The porch. The chair I built wrong twice before it held weight. Coffee — or whatever the local equivalent is, dark and bitter, bought from the village three weeks ago.

The fog lifts. The valley opens up. Green hills, a creek at the bottom, the treeline where the blackberry bear used to live. Quiet. The kind of quiet that took three months to stop feeling wrong.

The ember banks low. The nodachi leans against the door frame. The book from the peddler sits open on the arm of the chair, page down, spine cracked. I haven't turned a page in an hour.

No Whisper Stones humming. No construct network pulsing. No Garrett knocking. No NPC asking something, needing something, wanting something.

Just the creek. The wind. The valley.

Day 229. Nothing happens. That's the point.

---

The bag of holding swallows the old life. Emberfrost. The leather. The ring. The bracelet. All of it goes into the dark and weighs nothing.

I lock the Hearthstead door. Not that anyone's coming. The garden needs water. It'll keep.

---

Four miles of dirt road through the valley floor. Late morning sun on the fields. A cart track worn into the grass by farmers who've been using it longer than Varenholm has had an Academy.

The hakama moves quiet. The boots leave no prints. The nodachi rides my hip. Hat low. Mask up. Hazel eyes on the road.

Nobody passes me. A hawk circles the eastern ridge. The creek runs parallel to the road for the first two miles, then cuts west toward someone's irrigation. Sheep on a hillside. A dog barks once from a farmhouse and stops.

---

Greymere village. Maybe two hundred people. A crossroads — north toward the highland passes, south toward the trade roads that eventually connect to Crestfall if you walk long enough. One inn. A general store. A smithy that doubles as a farrier. A temple to something local. A baker. A well in the square.

Mid-morning. A handful of people in the square. A woman hauling water. Two old men on a bench. A kid chasing a chicken. A merchant's cart outside the general store — just arrived, canvas still tied down.

The inn sign reads *The Stubborn Mule*. The door's open.

---

The Stubborn Mule smells like stew and lamp oil. Low ceiling. Five tables. A bar with stools that don't match. The innkeeper — a thick man with a red nose and flour on his apron — looks up when the door opens. Decides I'm not his problem. Goes back to wiping the bar.

Two farmers at a corner table. A merchant woman eating bread alone. An old man nursing something dark by the window.

I take a stool. Order cider.

The merchant woman is talking to the farmers. Quiet voice — but the room is small.

"—won't take the south road anymore. Not worth the contract." She tears bread. Chews. "Thornfield's done. Three caravans turned back this season. The last driver who pushed through said the road itself was wrong — webs across the path, things moving in the treeline in broad daylight. He didn't stop. Didn't deliver. Came back white as milk."

The older farmer leans in. "My cousin had a plot south of there. Barley farm. Packed up two months ago. Said the soil went dead overnight. Not dry — *dead*. Cold to the touch. Nothing would take."

The other farmer shakes his head. "Millhaven sent men. Six soldiers. Three weeks ago."

A pause.

"And?"

"And nothing. They didn't come back. Millhaven isn't sending more."

The merchant pushes her plate away. "There's a woman down there — some mage — bought a farm right before it all went bad. They say her land is the only green thing left on that side of the village. Walls of vine. Nothing gets through. But she doesn't leave her property. Doesn't help anyone else. Just sits behind her plants and watches the village rot."

---

I pick up the cider and move to the merchant's table. The two farmers go quiet. Three sets of eyes on the hat, the mask, the nodachi.

I set the cider down. Sit without asking.

Her name is Breca. Runs dry goods between Greymere, Millhaven, and — until recently — Thornfield. She talks like someone billing you by the minute.

"Last delivery I made was eleven weeks ago. Feed grain. Took the south road, normal run, two days." She taps the table. "Webs. Across the road. Thick. Ropy. Chest-height. And the smell — like turned meat and something chemical underneath."

The older farmer — Oren, her uncle — talks about his cousin Hal. Barley farm south of Thornfield. Beetles through the soil. Entire field dead in two days. Packed up. Gone.

The younger farmer's sister is in Thornfield still. Temple is safe — the priest's ground doesn't get the corruption. But she said something came out of the forest in daylight last month. Bigger than a horse. Stood at a fence line. Looking.

Breca tells me about the Broodmother. The herbalist named Wynn who maps the corruption. The mage who grows her tomatoes behind a vine wall while the village rots.

The Millhaven soldiers — six armed men, garrison-trained. Three weeks. Nothing.

She hands me a map. Trade route markings. Distance notes.

"The road forks at the Stonecross marker. Left goes to Millhaven. Right goes to Thornfield. You'll know you're close when the trees start leaning."

She pauses.

"Don't cut the webs."

---

I buy a room and a round. Breca stays for an hour. She tells me more about the route, the village, the slow death of a place she delivered to for nine years.

Halfway through the second ale she undoes the top two buttons of her collar. Not looking at me. Looking at the fire.

*"Warm in here."*

It is not warm in here.

A few minutes later her boot nudges mine under the table and stays there. She starts telling me she hasn't liked a man's face in six years and my face, she is warning me now, is on her list. She is saying it flat, with the same tone she used to describe the webs, which is the funniest part.

She leaves fast when the ale is gone. Pushes the chair in hard. Gives me the map at the door.

*"I'm in the yard. Cart with the red axle. I'll be there a while if you've got anything else to ask me."*

She does not mean the map.

---

Later. The copper tub. She came back — because she wanted to, and she said so at the door. Widow, six years on her own, a ronin she liked the face of passing through the only village she still delivered to. She told me at the threshold she was done being coy about it.

In the tub she laughed once at something I said and it surprised her — she put a hand over her mouth like she'd forgotten the sound. She had opinions about where my hands went. She gave them.

Afterwards, she dressed with her back to me. Steady hands. Every buckle a piece of armor going back on.

At the door she stopped. Half a smile.

*"I'm going to drive north. I'm going to tell the next village I stopped for the bottle. I'm not sorry, ronin. Come through Fallowmere again and I'll stop for you first."*

Cart wheels on gravel. Gone.

---

### Day 230-231 — South Road to Thornfield

---

Dawn. The south road.

Road Sense kicks in before I reach the fork. The north road toward Millhaven pulses warm — traffic, life. The south road is cold. A thread with nothing on it. Dead trade route.

The Long Haul settles into my legs. Two days of walking feels like a morning stroll. I don't stop. Don't eat. Don't need to.

---

Day one. Normal road. Packed earth, wheel ruts, wildflowers. Nobody in either direction.

Night falls. I walk through it. The boots leave no prints. The stars turn overhead and the road unspools south and I don't feel a mile of it.

Day two. Afternoon. The Stonecross marker — weathered granite at the fork. Someone scratched into the stone with a knife, recent:

*DONT GO SOUTH*

I go south.

---

The last mile. Breca was right.

The trees lean in. Reaching, not blowing — the trunks curve toward the road. The canopy closes overhead. The light changes. Gets grey. The air smells damp and chemical and sweet in a way that's wrong.

Webs. Across the road. Chest-height. I don't cut them. I step around. Six webs in a quarter mile.

Then chimney smoke. Faint. The trees open up.

---

### Thornfield

---

Half of it is empty. The eastern side — boarded windows, sagging fences, silence. Webs on everything east of the main road. A farmhouse with its door open. A barn with the roof caved.

The western side is alive. Barely. Smoke from chimneys. A man repairing a fence with his back to the treeline. Children near the well — close to it. Tethered to it.

The temple at the village center has people outside it. Sitting, not worshipping. Blankets. Cook fires. A refugee camp in the yard of a harvest god.

The tavern. Green door. Faded sign. *Delia's.* Still open.

---

Inside. Four people. Three sharing a bowl of stew and a heel of bread. An old man asleep in the corner. No coin on the tables. The stew pot over the hearth is thin — more water than meat. Delia is feeding people, not serving them.

Delia. Broad. Ruddy-cheeked. Arms like she kneads dough and carries kegs. But hollowed out. Dark circles. Ten years older than her age.

I put five gold on the bar. In Thornfield right now, that's a fortune.

"Get us a room with privacy and honey mead. I heard the rumors. Breca sent me."

She stares at the gold like she's checking if the words are real. Two coins go in her apron. Three go to the stew fund.

---

The back room. She brings a bottle she's been saving. Dark amber glass, wax seal intact. Pours two measures. Sits across from me. I take off my shirt, sit back on the couch, and close my eyes.

"Talk," I say. "Tell me everything."

She tells me everything.

Six months of a village dying by inches. The webs. The livestock kills. The coordination. The mage who came and stayed and stopped. The Broodmother. The daytime swarms. Tom Buckley's farm gone in an hour. Delia at the mage's gate saying *people are going to die* and the gate closing. The Millhaven soldiers — six men, twenty-one days, nothing.

Forty people left in the first months. Then twenty more. Then ten. Father Crewe's temple yard as refugee camp. Wynn the herbalist mapping a corruption she can't fight. Harwick filling his logbook with a record of failure.

And Delia. Stretching turnip stew into its third day. Keeping the green door open because closing it means admitting it's over.

"Nobody came," she says. The voice of a woman who held a village together for six months with stew and stubbornness. "Until you."

I tell her I'm going to save her inn. I tell her to see Wynn in the morning.

She leaves. Goes back to her stew pot. Feeds her people. That's what Delia does.

---

### Day 231 — Dawn — Wynn's Cottage

---

South end of the village. The herb garden is the only thing in Thornfield that looks like it belongs to a different season. Raised beds. Trellises. A drying rack. The greenhouse. And at the far eastern edge — dead beds, quarantine borders, the corruption pressing close.

Wynn. Late thirties. Lean. Sun-darkened. Short dark hair. Calloused hands. She feels me before she sees me.

"Delia sent you." Not a question.

Three hours. Mask off. She walks me through six months of data. The corruption map. The ley lines — three, converging deep in the Greenveil. The creature patrol patterns charted at dawn and dusk for weeks. Soil samples in labeled jars — healthy on the left, corrupted on the right. Dead beetles pinned to a board with purple-black veining under a magnifying lens. Charts. Timelines. The small precise script getting less steady on the recent pages.

She marks my map. The treeline. The creek — webrot moss source. The patrol rings. The Broodmother's range. The old logging road. The red circle at the center of the Greenveil with a question mark inside.

"The source is in there. Three miles in, maybe more. Whatever is generating the corruption sits at the convergence."

She tells me about Amaris. The druid who could have purified the ley lines. Who went into the forest once, killed two sentries, and never went back.

"Delia is upset because she stopped believing anyone was coming," Wynn says. "And now you're here and she's terrified you'll do the same thing."

---

### Briarstone Homestead

---

Twenty minutes east. Every step the land gets worse. Overgrown to grey to dead. Cold through the boot soles. Abandoned farms on both sides. Webs on everything.

Then — green. Violent, defiant, impossible green in the middle of a wasteland. Twelve acres of life surrounded by death.

The bittervine wall is six months mature. Eight feet tall. Amber sap catching the morning light. Behind it — crops. Rows of green. The farmhouse patched. The barn standing straight. Smoke from the chimney.

A voice from the barn roof.

"That's close enough."

---

Amaris. Silver-white hair. Green eyes. Five-three and sitting on the roof peak with a double-bladed scimitar across her knees, looking down at me the way a cat looks at something that wandered into its yard.

"The village sent you. Delia? Harwick? Wynn with her charts? Whichever one, the answer's the same. I protect my land. The forest is not my problem."

She drops off the roof. We go inside. I bring out food from the bag of holding — Silver Draft roast pork, herbed potatoes, honeyed carrots, sourdough. She stares at it. Then eats like someone remembering what real food tastes like.

"If you're trying to bribe me it's working."

Three hours. She tells me everything. The Academy. Fifteen years growing things for people who didn't care. The stipend savings. The listing. *Exceptional soil.* Maren's shaking hands. The spiders. The thrown scimitar. The miss.

The bittervine wall. The ley line purification under her own farm — one-third of the corruption's supply severed. The two visits from Wynn she couldn't act on. The daytime swarm she watched from her roof. Delia at her gate. The Millhaven soldiers marching past with a nod. The combat sounds from the forest. Then clicking. Then nothing.

"I'm one person. I grow things. And everything out there wants to kill what I grow."

She identified the aura at the first hour. Siren-Elf charm awareness. She handled it the way she handles everything — out loud.

"You're unreasonably attractive and I'm furious about it."

---

I tell her I need her help. Her druid magic. I'll handle the monsters. She walks behind me and fixes the ground.

"That's the plan?"

"Tonight we hunt."

---

The afternoon. The narrow couch in her farmhouse. Her back against my chest. The silver hair against my collarbone. She reaches back, finds me, guides me in, and stays. Connected. Not moving. Just breathing.

"Don't move yet. Just — stay."

Eight months of empty. Six of them alone on a farm surrounded by nightmares. She held position for a long time. Then her hips started. Slow. Small. Building it at her own pace.

She slept connected. Still pressed against me. The first real sleep in months. The afternoon light moving across the floor.

She woke with the light going gold. Separated slowly. Stood. Didn't look at me for a full minute.

Then the armor. Buckle by buckle.

"I don't know your name."

"Kenji. The ronin. Wandering warrior."

"Kenji." She tested it. "I'm going to think about that name at inappropriate times for the rest of my life."

---

### Day 231 — Dusk — The Barn Roof

---

Both of us flat on our stomachs. The Greenveil treeline fifty yards away. Dusk settling.

Living Ground — new, inherited from the bond — reads through the warden's root network. Every inch of Briarstone alive with information. The bittervine wall humming. The healthy soil. And beyond the property line — cold, dead ground crawling with movement.

The clicking starts.

Six shapes at the treeline. Waist-high spiders. Purple-black veining. Moving in pairs. Patrol formation. They approach the bittervine wall. Test it. Retreat. Spread along the perimeter.

Then the ground vibration. Heavy. Rhythmic. The treeline parts.

The Broodmother.

Wagon-sized. Legs like tree trunks. Abdomen pulsing with corruption so thick it looks like it's wearing her. Multiple eye clusters catching the last light. Mandibles the length of my arm.

On her back — a dozen smaller spiders. Riders. Juveniles. A mobile deployment platform.

She stands at the treeline. Watches the farmhouse with eyes that reflect the bittervine's amber glow. Two full minutes. Then turns. Walks back into the Greenveil. The ground shakes.

Amaris is rigid beside me. Her hand on my forearm. White-knuckled. Her breathing fast and shallow.

"That's her. That's what I've been watching from this roof for six months."

The clicking fades. The sentries follow the Broodmother into the dark.

Amaris rolls onto her back. Stares at the sky.

"Still want to hunt?"

---

End of Fraying Empire — Chapter One: *Greymere*

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter Two: *The Greenveil*

### Day 232 — Dawn — Briarstone Homestead

---

Dawn. Grey light through the shutters. The clicking has stopped. The sentries have pulled back.

Amaris is already up. Armored. Pack loaded. Bittervine cuttings, webrot moss vials, pale sage bundles, warden's root seeds, component pouch, scimitar on her back. She's standing at the kitchen table eating cold soup with one hand and checking her supplies with the other.

The south gate. The gap in the bittervine wall. Beyond it — grey dead farmland and the dark line of the Greenveil a hundred yards east.

Morning light hits the treeline. The leaning trunks cast long shadows. No movement. No clicking. The window is open.

Amaris stands at the gate. Looks at the forest. Her hands are shaking. She grips the gate post until they stop.

"Okay." One breath. "Okay."

She steps through.

---

### The Logging Road

---

The old cart ruts are barely visible under dead undergrowth. Wide enough for two people. Packed earth under the rot. Heading northeast into the canopy.

The forest closes around us. The canopy cuts the light to grey-green murk within thirty yards. The temperature drops. The chemical sweet smell is immediate — stronger than the road, stronger than the treeline.

Living Ground activates through the root systems under my boots. The trees are alive but wrong — root networks twisted, sap running dark. The soil is cold. Sick, not dead yet — the logging road is on the southern edge.

Amaris feels it too. "The soil here is corrupted but salvageable." She speaks low. Marks a mental note. Keeps walking.

---

Fifteen minutes. Half a mile. The logging road curves east. Dead ferns, grey moss, webs in the upper canopy. Thin ones. Old. Perimeter markers.

A funnel web between two trees. Silk tube disappearing into a hollow trunk. Empty. Daytime.

Amaris: "Silk Lurker nest. Ambush predator. Nocturnal. We're fine."

A pause.

"We're fine *right now*."

---

### The Creek Crossing

---

Thirty minutes. The logging road intersects a shallow stream. Clear water over smooth stones. Patches of pale green-grey moss on the rocks.

Webrot moss. Same creek Amaris harvested on Day 1. Growth is thicker now — six months undisturbed.

She kneels at the bank. Cutting. Hands steady. This part she knows.

On the trunk of an oak ten feet above — claw marks. Eight parallel grooves. Fresh. Something large climbed this tree recently and sat looking down at the water.

Amaris sees it. "Those marks weren't here six months ago. The sentries were dog-sized. Whatever made those is —"

She measures the spacing with her eyes.

"Bigger."

---

### The Silk Lurker Colony

---

I hand her the map. Tell her to keep going. Check every point Wynn marked. I'll be nearby in stealth.

"Did you just call me —"

Wind Step. Silent. Gone. The canopy above the logging road, twenty feet up.

Amaris stands alone at the creek crossing holding a map and a scimitar, staring at the empty space where I was.

"I hate him," she says to nobody.

She's smiling.

---

I shadow her from the canopy. She navigates well. The Academy taught her maps and the forest taught her soil.

The Silk Lurker colony — sixty feet of funnel webs strung between dead trees. Wynn counted twelve nests in Month 3. Amaris counts twenty-three. I count twenty-five from above. Two she missed — high canopy, bigger than the ones below.

"Nearly doubled," she says. Marks the map.

She's through the corridor in five minutes. Doesn't touch a thread.

---

### The Dead Zone

---

One mile in. The soil transitions. Behind her — sick but alive. Ahead — finished. Root networks ending like they were cut. Trees standing but hollow.

Amaris kneels. Palm flat on the soil.

"Nothing. The ley line under this stretch isn't corrupted. It's *drained*. The energy is being pulled toward the center. The soil didn't die from poison. It died from starvation."

She marks the map. Stands. Her face is pale.

"My feet hurt."

She keeps going.

---

### The Millhaven Soldiers

---

One and a half miles. The creek intersects the logging road. The water is grey now.

She smells it before she sees it.

Webbed to the trees. Both sides of the creek. Six cocoons — man-sized, wrapped in grey silk so thick the shapes are barely human. Armor fragments on the ground. A shield with Millhaven's crest. A sword still in its scabbard. A boot standing upright in the creek bed like someone set it there neatly.

One cocoon is open. Split at the chest. Drag marks leading deeper into the forest.

Amaris sits on a rock. Hard. The map in her lap. She breathes through her mouth.

"They came in a straight line. Standard military. Fastest path." Her voice is thin. "Something pulled one out. Fed on it. Or took it somewhere."

She marks the map. Her charcoal hand is unsteady.

She doesn't stand up for a full minute.

---

### The Lurker Colony — Clearing

---

I drop from the canopy. Tell her to start destroying the colony. I'll kill whatever wakes up.

She does the math. Pale sage smoke drives them out disoriented. Earthen Command collapses the funnels. They come out blind.

She lights the sage. Holds it high. 

"Earthen Command."

The ground erupts. Three nests collapse simultaneously. Silk tears. Funnels implode. Sage smoke pours into the gaps.

Three lurkers spill out. Legs scrambling. Eyes clouded. Stumbling blind.

The nodachi leaves the scabbard.

First lurker. Draw. Red-black steel through the crown to the abdomen. Dead before it hits the ground.

Second lurker. The return stroke. Abyssal edge hums — red-black light flaring once. The lurker dissolves. Vaporized. Nothing left but dark motes rising in the sage smoke.

Third lurker. Running. Not fast enough. The blade finds it mid-stride.

The nodachi rises in a slow arc over the right shoulder. Tip skyward. Rotates down behind the back. Slides home. *Shhhhiiiing.* Click.

Three lurkers in four seconds.

Amaris doesn't stop. South to north. Five nests at a time. The sage smoke everywhere. Lurkers spilling out blind and panicked.

Four more hit open ground. Wind Step — silent landing. The nodachi drawn.

First: draw-strike. Dead. Second: follow-through. Vaporized — red-black motes drifting like dark snow. Third: pivot. Dead. Fourth: return stroke. Wounded. A second cut finishes it.

The blade flips in my hand. Full rotation. Red-black steel catching the dim light for one second. The edge finds the scabbard mouth blind. Click.

Seven lurkers. Eighteen nests collapsed.

The upper canopy nests. The big ones. Wind Step to the branches. The first lurker senses me a half-second before the draw. Half a beat too late.

The nest dissolves with the occupant. Silk, chitin, branch — all of it becoming particulate. Dark snow through the canopy.

The second lurker bolts. Punches through its own silk and launches down the trunk. I'm faster. Clean kill. It hits the ground in two pieces.

One sharp flick — the blade snaps horizontal. Nothing to clean. The abyssal edge doesn't hold anything. Slide. Click. Silence.

Twenty-five nests. Destroyed. Fourteen lurkers killed. Eleven absent — deeper in the forest.

Amaris stands in the wrecked corridor. Sage smoke drifting. Looking at the vaporization marks.

"What the *hell* kind of wandering warrior are you?"

---

### Inner Ring — Amaris Solo

---

We fall into step. Shoulder to shoulder.

"The kind that satisfies you on your couch."

Her mouth opens. Closes. The flush hits her ears.

"I hate you."

She doesn't hate me.

---

The inner patrol ring. Four silk hammocks in the canopy. Each spider bigger than a large dog. Darker chitin. Deeper veining. The garrison.

I tell her to take them. I'll step in if needed.

She stares. She calculates. She does it.

Sage smoke first. Webrot on the low hammocks. Entangle — the thorned roots from Day 1, meaner now, climbing the trunks and finding the shapes inside the dissolving silk.

Two spiders pinned and pierced in the canopy. A third drops — she catches it with Earthen Command, flips it on its back, drives the scimitar into the exposed underbelly. Twice. Dead.

The fourth drops on her. Full weight. Mandibles snapping. She holds them open with the scimitar crossguard. Legs wrapping her body. The bite gets through — shoulder, through the leather. The venom hits. Paralysis. She goes down.

She grows roots through her own back. Through the spider above her. Thorned runners punching through the abdomen from below. It staggers off. She rolls free. Drives the blade through the eye cluster.

The remaining two in the canopy — she brings the branches down with Earthen Command. Walks through the wreckage. The scimitar rising and falling. Methodical. Every strike placed. Joint between thorax and abdomen. Eye cluster. Underbelly.

Four dead spiders. Purple ichor on everything. Blood on her arm from the bite.

"I just killed four giant spiders."

---

### The Stilthorn Recipe

---

She asks how big the spiders are going to get. I tell her I brought something for her — a paralytic recipe from a master herbalist. Stilthorn. Three-second onset. Full motor paralysis. One minute.

She reads it at INT 16 speed and almost drops it.

"Whoever wrote this was doing field refinement without lab equipment. This is grandmaster-level work." She stares at me. "You have INT 9 and someone handed you this and you just *kept it in your bag?*"

She tucks the recipe into her component pouch like it's worth more than gold. It is.

"If I'd had this twenty minutes ago I wouldn't have almost died."

---

### The Short Rest

---

The creek crossing. Running water. Healthier soil. She heals herself — Cure Wounds on the mandible wound. Grinds a poultice. Drinks. Eats.

I tell her we're not heading back. Short rest. She won't need to fight. I'll take the big one.

"Good job taking out those four. I had complete faith in you."

She looks at me. Nobody's said good job to her in six months.

"Were you actually scared?" she asks. "When that last one was three feet from me?"

I tell her I wanted her to have the victory. She earned it. But I'd never let anything hurt her.

She leans into me. The ichor-covered armor against my chest. The silver hair against my neck.

"Nobody's said that to me either. The not letting anything hurt me part."

---

Thirty minutes into the rest. I pick her up. She lifts the mage robe. Her back against the bark. Brief. Intense. Her face against my neck.

When I finish, something slips. A thread of gold warmth through my hands and into her body. The ember — just a whisper. The remaining wounds close. The venom purges. The exhaustion lifts.

But more than that. Something deeper. The Lover's Vigor settles into her like sunlight into soil. Every stat shifting. Every sense sharpening. The scimitar that was always a little too heavy suddenly feels like nothing.

She gasps. Pulls back. Looks at her own hands.

She crushes a rock with her bare fingers. Stares at the pebbles falling out of her fist.

*"Okay. Okay, what the hell was that."*

Not scared. Delighted and completely confused at the same time. She jumps — six feet straight up, lands in a crouch, silent, balanced. She draws the scimitar. It moves like a willow switch.

*"My spells are stronger. I can think faster. I memorized the Stilthorn recipe from one reading."* She turns to me, grinning now, eyes wide. *"Ronin. What ARE you."*

I tell her I came inside of her.

She laughs — loud, real, echoes off the web canopy.

*"That is NOT why I can CRUSH ROCKS with my BARE HANDS. Try again. With more words."*

She has questions. I tell her after the big one.

"INT. Nine. I'm sleeping with a man who has the emotional communication skills of a fence post."

---

### The Broodmother's Nest

---

The web canopy thickens into a ceiling. The clicking is everywhere. The nesting chamber opens ahead — forty-foot depression, silk walls, floor, ceiling. And in the center —

The Broodmother. Wagon-sized. Legs like tree trunks. Abdomen pulsing corruption so dense it looks structural. Thirty juveniles on her back. Two hundred egg sacs on the walls. Asleep.

Amaris can feel all of it now. WIS 25. The Broodmother's weight. The juveniles' legs. The things in the eggs twitching.

"That's not a spider. That's a building with legs."

I go invisible. Smoke bomb. The phantom double leaps into the canopy — a copy of the ronin crouching on a branch.

Amaris stares at the illusion. "I *think* I know that's not really you."

She looks at the nest. INT 24 working. The plan builds in seconds.

"The silk is the infrastructure. Webrot dissolves silk. I don't have enough webrot for the whole chamber — but I can *grow* more."

Twenty minutes at the creek. Bloom Touch. Webrot moss carpets spreading across every stone. She harvests in handfuls. Grinds it with sage ash into a compound. Packs three clay pots. Seals them with wax.

Field-expedient area-denial weapons made from creek moss and dried herbs by a Level 5 druid with INT 24 and a grudge.

"Sage bomb. Thirty-foot radius. Everything silk dissolves. Spiders go blind. Eggs collapse. Floor fails."

---

She stands at the chamber entrance. Three clay pots on her belt. The scimitar drawn.

The first sage bomb arcs into the center. Clay shatters. White-grey smoke erupts. The silk floor hisses. Dissolves. Sags.

Second bomb. Left wall. Forty egg sacs collapse — silk pouches disintegrating, contents spilling onto webbing that's already gone.

Third bomb. Right wall. Same result. The smoke fills the chamber. Every strand of silk coming apart.

The juveniles wake into chaos. No floor. No vibration sense. Thirty of them scrambling off the Broodmother's back in every direction. Tumbling. Blind.

The Broodmother wakes. The massive body lurches. The eye clusters open. The mandibles spread. A sound that isn't clicking — deeper, a vibration through the dead soil.

The floor gives. She falls. Through the dissolved silk, into the tunnels below. The ground shakes on impact. Massive legs finding stone and scrambling — going deeper. Away from the smoke. Toward the Nexus.

Amaris steps into the chamber.

"Entangle."

---

The roots come up thorned and furious. WIS 25 through dead soil. Six juveniles in the first burst. Five pinned. One impaled through the thorax.

She walks through her own Entangle zone — the roots part for her — and starts cutting. The scimitar rising and falling. Clinical. Joint between thorax and abdomen. Eye cluster. Underbelly. Every strike placed.

Second Entangle. L2 slot. Eight more pinned. Eight more killed. The scimitar dripping. The Academy mage applying the same precision she learned memorizing parasitic vines to spider anatomy.

Fifteen juveniles dead. Fifteen fled into the forest — they'll go feral without the nest. Two hundred egg sacs dissolved. The Broodmother's infrastructure destroyed.

Amaris stands in the center of the ruined chamber. Smoke drifting. The silk ceiling gone. Grey light falling into the wreckage.

She looks at the tunnel opening where the Broodmother fell through. The dark goes deep.

She looks at the illusion in the canopy.

"Your future baby mama just leveled your nursery."

---

End of Fraying Empire — Chapter Two: *The Greenveil*

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter Three: *Stillday*

### Ashmere 11-18, 1247 AR — Thornfield

---

The Greenveil is done. The Nexus is dead. The Broodmother is composting in a tunnel full of ferns. The ley lines run clean and the soil is waking up and Amaris is Level 16 and standing in a ruined chamber looking for a man who's already gone.

I don't reappear. The smoke bomb illusion fades in the tunnel. I take a side passage. Wind Step through the dying forest that isn't dying anymore. Across the dead farmland that's already starting to feel different underfoot.

The Stubborn Mule. Delia's tavern. The green door.

"Room. Privacy. One week."

---

### The Week

---

Seven days in a back room. Draw, strike, sheathe. The nodachi whispering through the air a thousand times. The ember quiet. The Whisper Stone off.

Living Ground reads the village through the floorboards. The soil healing. The clicking gone from the treeline. Day by day Thornfield starts to breathe again.

Through the wall — fragments. Delia's voice. Villagers returning.

"—the druid killed it. In the cave. Alone."

"—walked in there and—"

"—what about that swordsman? The one in the mask?"

"—gone. Just gone."

---

Amaris doesn't come to the inn. She went back to Briarstone. She checks the logging road. The creek crossing. The barn roof. The couch.

Nothing. No prints. No tracks. Windstrider boots.

She sits at the kitchen table. The couch still smells like him. Root Network searches for a heartbeat through a mile of healing soil.

She doesn't find it.

---

### Delia

---

Delia comes to the back room on the third day with fresh bread she baked that morning. The food tray stays in the hall. Two cups. A bottle of honey mead — a trader came through, the first in two months.

"My people don't need me this morning." She sits on the edge of the bed. "The stew has beef. Tom is fixing his own fence. Twelve people last night."

She looks at me.

"Last time I chose the stew pot. I'd choose it again. But this morning I'm choosing breakfast."

---

She's different from the first night. She's not the woman holding a dying village together with turnip stew and stubbornness. The weight is gone. What's left is a forty-three-year-old woman with broad shoulders who kneads dough and pours ale and decided to bring two cups upstairs.

She takes her time. Forty-three years of knowing herself. She laughs once — at the situation, at herself, at the fact that she's in the back room of her own inn.

"I run a *tavern*. I kneaded *bread* this morning."

---

She comes back every morning after that. Real eggs. Warm bread. Tea. She sits for an hour. Sometimes she stays longer. She doesn't ask about the mask or the sword or where I'm going.

On the last morning she stands at the door.

"Breakfast in an hour. The eggs are for you. Not the tray-outside-the-door eggs. The real ones."

A pause. Softer.

"Thank you for letting me choose this time."

---

### Wynn

---

Ashmere 18. The last day. South end of the village. The herb garden that's the only thing in Thornfield that's always looked alive. Now the rest of the village is catching up.

She's in the garden. Kneeling between rows. She feels me at the gate.

"You're leaving." Not a question.

I tell her I'm glad her door is open. Ask if I can spend the night. I want to watch her garden and hear about Stillday.

"You want to watch my garden."

"Yeah."

"And hear about Stillday."

"I don't know what it is."

That stops her. She files it somewhere different from the aura notes. The place where she keeps things that don't fit.

"Everyone knows what Stillday is. Children know what Stillday is."

She opens the door wider.

---

She cooks while she talks. Moves between the stove and the cutting board with the efficiency of a woman who's lived alone long enough to make the kitchen a single-person choreography.

"Stillday is the sixth day. The rest day. Five days of work, one of still. Temples open. Shops close. Families eat together."

She tells me about the calendar. The seasons. The months I didn't know had names. Seedmere. Bright Turn. Rainmarch. The words for the time I've been living in without knowing how to count it.

She tells me about Harvest Week — the biggest event of the year, which happened while I was alone in a valley. About the Long Day — tournament season, which happened while Sera sat in a house she bought with champion's gold. About the Still Night — the winter solstice. The one about family and warmth and saying the things you've been carrying.

"How do you not know this? Where are you *from?*"

---

Night. The garden by greenhouse light. She walks me through every row. What grows where and why. The thornmint. The pale sage. The eastern beds with new growth where corruption used to live.

"I spent six months watching that treeline and being afraid. Now I watch it and I hear crickets. Normal crickets. The real kind."

She's quiet for a moment.

"That's because of you."

---

Inside. Late. She stands at her bedroom door. Hand on the frame.

"I'm not going to ask you to come to my room. Not because I don't want to. But I'm choosing to stand here and say goodnight because that's the version of me I want to be."

She turns. The hazel eyes steady.

"But if you knock, I'll answer."

The door closes.

I strip down. Walk to the washroom.

"Where can I wash these? And where'd you want me to sleep?"

The door opens. Wynn in the sleep shift. She stares.

"The — there's a basin. In the — the washroom is —"

She points at a door she's walked through ten thousand times and cannot name.

"You're standing in my kitchen. Naked. Asking about laundry."

---

She comes to wash me. The soap on the right. Calloused hands and soil under the nails. Clinical for thirty seconds. Then not.

"I've been alone for three years. The work was more interesting than anyone available."

Her forehead against the back of my shoulder. Her hands still on my chest.

"I can't manage this."

The filing system closes. Deliberately. The way she'd close a notebook when the experiment changes direction.

She steps into the tub.

"You knocked."

---

### Morning — Ashmere 19

---

She's been awake for an hour. Notebook open. Pencil in hand. Page eight.

"My grip strength has increased by approximately forty percent. I appear to have gained functional darkvision. My resting heart rate has dropped twelve beats per minute."

She holds up her hand. Opens and closes the fist.

"Something you do — during intimacy — changes the person you're with. Physically. Measurably."

I tell her all I remember is coming inside of her and her enjoying it.

She stares at me. Picks up the pencil.

"Chapter five. 'The Subject Has An INT of 9 And It Shows.'"

---

She suggests the mechanism is biological. Delivered through intimate contact. I suggest she collect a sample for study. She agrees. For science.

She has two labeled vials by mid-morning. *Sample A — in situ, activated.* *Sample B — oral extraction, unactivated.* In her small precise handwriting. On her shelf between the thornmint and the beetle specimens.

"Sample A has a faint luminescence. Gold-green. Sample B does not. The activation occurs during sustained internal contact."

She's written ten pages. She has charts.

"This is the most important discovery of my career and I collected it on my knees in my own kitchen."

---

I leave a clone nodding at her explanations. Smoke bomb under the table. Greater Invisibility. The phantom double sits in my chair, tilting its head attentively while Wynn describes luminescence decay rates.

She'll figure it out in ten minutes. The clone doesn't breathe.

She's going to be furious. Then she's going to write about it.

---

### The Crossroads

---

South road out of Thornfield. Ashmere 19. Windday. First frost on the ground. The road crunches underfoot.

Diagnostic Touch is live — every plant I brush feeds information. Living Ground reads healthy soil ahead. Road Sense traces the trade routes in every direction. Faint warmth south. Cold north. Distant warmth east. Nothing west.

Four roads. Frost on the ground. The treeline behind me stands straight for the first time in a year.

Thornfield is going to live. Amaris is Level 16 on a farm with legendary soil. Delia is planning Stillday seating. Wynn has two vials and ten pages of notes and a clone that doesn't breathe sitting at her kitchen table.

The Still Night is twenty-six days away. The holiday about family and warmth and saying the things you've been carrying. Wynn told me about it yesterday over stew.

I've been in this world for eight months and I've never celebrated a holiday.

The ronin walks.

---

End of Fraying Empire — Chapter Three: *Stillday*

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter Four: *Millhaven*

### Ashmere 19-22, 1247 AR — South Road & Millhaven

---

### The Road

---

Otten Dray. Dry goods. Flour, salt, lamp oil. Eleven years on the Millhaven circuit. Two mules, a cart, a crossbow, and a dog that sleeps through everything.

Three silver a day for a guard. I take the bench. The dog sniffs my boot. Decides I'm acceptable.

Two days south. The road is good — packed earth, moderate traffic. Autumn farmland turning gold and copper. The first frost came and went. The puddles have thin ice at dawn.

A boar in the road. Hour one. Big. Three hundred pounds. Diagnostic Touch reads it healthy from a hundred yards. It looks at the cart and decides we're not worth the trouble.

A stone marker off the road. Hour two. Old. Covered in moss. Living Ground reads something underneath — a foundation. Ancient. Pre-civilizational. The kind of stone nobody builds with anymore. Filed.

Wolves at the treeline. Hour five. Three of them calculating whether mules are worth the fight. They see the silhouette on the cart bench and leave. Whatever they read said *not worth it*.

Otten talks. Traders talk the way rivers flow — constant, low, following the path of least resistance. He tells me about Millhaven. About the soldiers who went to Thornfield and didn't come back. About the Ashenveil marshes. About the ArchMagus who vanished and the world falling apart.

"Strange times. The big hero disappears and the world starts falling apart. Almost like he was the only thing holding it together."

The fire pops. I don't answer.

Night camp behind a stone wall where traders have stopped for decades. Old fire rings. Watch rotation — I take first, Otten and the dog take second. Both watches clean. The road is quiet. The dog doesn't bark because there's nothing to bark at.

Women on the road. Ten over two days. Every one of them looks too long when we pass. Every one of them blinks and goes back to their conversation and forgets the masked swordsman by dinner. One farmer's wife — nat 20 — doesn't look twice. The world's highest compliment: being unremarkable to someone who's seen enough.

---

### The Gate

---

Millhaven. Stone walls on a hill. Four guards at a checkpoint. A queue. Otten pulls his trade license.

"Weapons check. All bladed weapons shown at the gate."

I hand the scabbarded nodachi to the female guard. She draws it for inspection. Stops halfway.

"What is this. The color is *in* the metal. This grain — crystalline. Like it was grown, not forged."

She finishes the draw. Examines it. Sheathes it. Hands it back. Her gauntlet brushes my hand.

"Peacebond it inside the walls."

She ties the cord. Close. Professional. Mostly.

I tell her drinks are on me after shift. Find me at the bar.

---

### Taryn

---

The Broken Wheel. Garrison tavern. Rough. Loud. I wait at the bar.

She walks in at seventh bell. Out of armor. Dark hair loose. Late twenties. Lean. The build of a woman who's drilled with a halberd since she was sixteen. A burn scar on her wrist. A scar across her eyebrow from something she doesn't talk about.

She sits down. Doesn't look at me yet. Orders ale. Drinks.

"I don't do this. I don't meet strangers at bars after shift. My name's Taryn."

Private room. Roast duck. Honey mead. She eats with her hands. Tears the wings off. Talks with her mouth full.

"Your blade's balanced wrong. Tip-heavy like that, you're committing everything to the first cut. If you miss, you're dead. Which means you don't miss."

She sucks the bone clean.

"Arm wrestle me."

---

I take her hand. She pushes. The arm that's beaten thirty-one garrison soldiers — men who outweigh her by sixty pounds — pushes with everything it has.

My arm doesn't move.

I don't push back. I hold her hand and look at her eyes. My thumb traces across her knuckles. I start talking. Casual. How long she's been a guard. What she knows about the area. Jobs that pay real money.

She keeps pushing for about twenty seconds. Then she stops pushing, looks at our hands, looks at my face, raises an eyebrow, and lets her grip soften — contest grip to just a grip. Holding on.

*"Oh,"* she says, half a smile. *"It's like that."*

I lower her arm slow while she tells me about the Ashenveil and the missing caravan and the wolves and the ruin. Her hand touches the table gentle. The softest pin. She leaves her hand in mine after.

*"Thirty-one and five,"* she says quiet. Grinning now. *"The other four losses made me angry. This one did not."*

---

### The Blacksmith

---

I tell her I want to buy her a polearm. The best one available.

"We've known each other for THREE HOURS—"

Holsk. Dwarven blacksmith. Garrison road. Four-foot-eight. Shoulders wider than the doorframe. He smells the abyssal shard nodachi from across the room.

"That's not standard steel in there. Crystalline lattice. Resonant alloy. Abyssal adjacent. Deep-forged."

He opens the door wider. Looks at Taryn. Reads her like metal — the calluses, the stance, the burn scar pulling the wrist, the half-second on the return stroke.

Custom commission. Mythril alloy. Rune-tempered. Three enchantment slots built into the crystal structure during forging. The weapon grows with the wielder. Forty gold. A week to forge.

I put the gold on the table.

Taryn stares at the lockbox where forty gold disappeared.

"Three hours. Three *hours*."

---

### The Inn

---

She takes the mask off herself. One hand. Quick. Looks at my face for two seconds.

*"Yeah. I'm keeping this. Just so we're clear."*

Fast. Hard. The bed frame hits the wall. She doesn't make noise — she breathes through exertion. The way she breathes through a drill.

After — she stretches her hand out, flexes the wrist, rotates it. Looks at the old burn scar. Rotates again. A slow grin starts.

*"Huh. My wrist doesn't hurt. It's hurt for eleven years. Ronin. What."*

She says it happy, not alarmed. Turns the wrist a third time. Laughs once.

---

Morning. The bed is in four pieces. Three noise complaints. A note from the innkeeper. Room 4 asked if the room is available tomorrow night.

I take her again. Longer. At three-quarters. After, she traces a hand down her own arm — the burn scar is smooth skin. The eyebrow is whole. The old ankle fracture. The shoulder. Eleven years of garrison wear gone. Her skin tightens. Two years of age easing backward.

"All of them. All of them are gone."

She catches her reflection in the washbasin water.

"I look twenty."

---

She runs morning drill for fifty recruits. I watch from the rooftop, invisible. The halberd moves like nothing Hadley has ever seen from a gate guard. Twelve forms. No hesitation. No compensation.

Hadley writes something in her book.

"Taryn. Your eyebrow—"

"*Don't ask.*"

---

Evening. Grilled lamb. Rice. Curry. Ironveil whiskey. Private room.

She gives me the map. Four jobs worth real money. The Ashenmere caravan — 150 gold. The Ashenveil scouting — 200 gold from Hadley. The wolf pack — 100 gold in bounties. The pre-kingdom ruin — unknown, ancient, sealed by Hadley after two scouts went down and one transferred to the coast.

"The ruin is either nothing or everything. That's why Hadley sealed it."

---

Bath. Tub. Not luxury — a wooden basin behind a curtain. She heats the water herself. She bought contraceptive herbs from the garrison road apothecary because she's a soldier and she's practical about everything.

Three times. She takes the tea. The ember slips small on the third.

"There it is. The warm thing."

---

Morning. Ashmere 22. She laces her boots in the dark.

I give her twenty gold.

"If you die in that ruin I'm going to find your body and kill you again."

She leaves for east gate duty. Bootfalls on the stairs. Quick. Even. No ankle. No wrist. The soldier she always should have been.

The ruin is south. The noon patrol gap opens in four hours.

---

End of Fraying Empire — Chapter Four: *Millhaven*

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter Five: *The Eastbound Run*

### Ashmere 23-24, 1247 AR — Millhaven & Beyond

---

Ashmere 22 I'd left the ruin south of Millhaven unopened — Hadley's seal, the noon window, Taryn on the wall expecting me to care about old stone before anything else. I didn't go. The letter from the bandit camp and the circle where ten wagons stopped existing both pointed east; the border the Lady drew wasn't where Hadley thought it was. East first. One night to sleep, then the road.

---

### The Eastbound Run

---

Dawn. Ashmere 23. Fieldday. I leave the Broken Wheel before first light. Smoke bomb in the alley. The clone takes the east gate at walking pace — the ronin heading out on business. I follow invisible, 120 feet behind. The aura doesn't fire. Nobody sees the real me. The ghost walks the road and the road doesn't notice.

Four hours east. The trade road thins. The farmsteads go dark. Shuttered. Abandoned. Nobody maintains this stretch anymore. Road Sense confirms — the trade warmth is dead. Whatever killed this route did it thoroughly.

---

Hour two. A shallow valley. Four men in the trees — leather, shortswords, a crossbow. Road bandits. Classic ambush. They step out and surround the clone.

"Stop. Weapons on the ground."

The clone bolts. Runs east. They chase. Four desperate men running after a ghost that doesn't breathe.

I loot the camp while they're gone. Twelve silver. A jade hairpin. A sealed letter — Ashenmere merchant house sigil, tower and crescent. Pocketed. Thirty seconds. No trace.

---

### The Caravan

---

Off-road. South of the east road. Living Ground finds the tracks — six sets of wagon ruts cutting through a harvested field. Loaded wagons cutting hard across stubble — running, no road.

The tracks stop. All six. Simultaneously. Like they hit a wall.

A sixty-foot circle of churned earth. Hooves. Boots. Something heavier. Signs of struggle. No bodies. No wagons. No horses. No cargo.

Ten people and six loaded wagons entered this circle three weeks ago and ceased to exist.

At the center — a post. Wooden. Sharpened. Black cloth at the base. A parchment nailed to it.

*The living pass through my borders carrying things that belong to the living. This is permitted. The living pass through my borders carrying weapons pointed at my domain. This is not.*

*Ten carried swords. Ten were collected. Their goods feed the March. Their horses pull the carts. Their bodies stand in the column.*

*— the Lady.*

The border isn't where Hadley thinks it is. It's here. Fifteen miles north. The Lady moved it.

---

### The Ashenveil

---

Three hours southeast. The road dies. The smell starts. The trees stunt. The mist rises. The Lady's border stakes — every thirty feet, black cloth, another note:

*Beyond this line the living serve or the living fall. There is no third option.*

I cross. Invisible. The clone leads.

Thirty minutes in — the root network reacts. Every dead root in a hundred feet twitches. A signal sent. She knows something entered — a living foot on a dead nerve. The shape of it she'll figure out later.

The column. Hundreds of them. Standing in knee-deep water. Man-shaped. Armor. Still as posts. Facing south. In formation. The dead of a hundred years waiting for orders. Among them — four skeletons in Millhaven garrison steel. Hadley's soldiers. The ones she sent to Thornfield. Walking patrol in the armor they died in.

I take what I can without touching the bodies. A shield — silver inlay, anti-turning ward. A ring — gold, blue stone, preservation enchantment. Pocketed.

---

A clearing. Higher ground. A fire in a stone ring. A death knight.

Sir Corwyn the Fallen. Black plate. Polished. A greatsword called Oathbreaker — Steel Sight reads it screaming. Two signatures in the metal. One holy. One necrotic. The sword is in pain.

He looks at the clone. Studies it.

"An image. Someone's sending projections into my lady's domain."

Behind the log — an iron chest. Warded. Pre-kingdom preservation enchantment. Something inside.

I move while he's talking to the ghost. Wind Step. Hands on the chest. STR 37 lifts it like air.

The handle creaks.

He hears it. Turns. The greatsword coming off the shoulder.

Tied initiative. I'm faster. Bag of Holding open. Chest goes in. Wind Step — seventy meters of swamp in one breath.

"THIEF."

The clone stays. Walks deeper into the marsh. Corwyn chases the ghost. The column reactivates. The root network fires. Everything in the Ashenveil chases a phantom south while I walk north.

Four hours of illusion duration. They can chase it until dusk.

I walk out. Invisible. Clean. The marsh behind me waking up and screaming at nothing.

---

### Holsk's Forge — Dawn, Ashmere 24

---

Stillday. The custom halberd is ready. The thrum wanted to be finished today — the metal did half of Holsk's work for him. Two hours for the final fold and the enchantment inscriptions.

Three runes. Featherfall. Truestrike. Bondseal. Thrum-alloy head on dark ash haft. The weapon hums when Taryn takes it.

She doesn't make a sound. She goes quiet. The kind of quiet that means something landed deeper than words.

Mythril-alloy half-plate. Refitted. Dark steel with blue-silver sheen. Holsk shaped the shoulders to her deltoids. The articulated joints move with her body.

She stands in Holsk's forge looking like something the war colleges draw in textbooks.

"Acceptable," Holsk says. From him, that's a love letter.

One hundred and five gold for the rush and the armor. Worth it.

---

### The Wolf Pack

---

I do the clone trick. The ronin spectating from a boulder with crossed arms. Invisible me watching from elsewhere.

The oak valley. Sixteen wolves. One warg matriarch. Three pups in a den.

Taryn takes the choke point. Plants the halberd. Whistles.

---

Round 1. Action Surge.

The wolves charge. The halberd sings. The thrum resonates on every stroke — a hum that vibrates the air after the blade passes through it.

The first wolf enters 15 feet. The pike point takes its skull. Reaper's Chain fires. The return stroke catches the next wolf mid-leap. Chain. The axe blade opens the third from shoulder to hip. Chain. The butt end cracks the fourth's ribs on the backstroke. Chain.

The chain doesn't stop. Every kill feeds the next swing. Every swing finds the next wolf. She's not fighting sixteen wolves — she's running a harvester through a corridor of fur and teeth and none of them can touch her. The choke compresses them and the 15-foot reach means they die before they reach her. Sixteen wolves. One round. Six seconds. The Reaper's Chain cascaded through every single one. The halberd sang sixteen times and every note was a death.

---

The Warg Matriarch. Alone. She howled but her pack was already dead.

Round 2. Polearm Defense. Free dodge. The Matriarch's bite found air. Taryn's halberd found flesh — three hits, two Grievous Wounds. The mythril edge opened the black fur and the cuts didn't close. Severe bleeding. Fifteen percent of max HP per turn. Per wound. Stacking.

Round 3. The Matriarch closed. Bit her. Clawed her. 36 damage. Taryn took it standing. Hit back. Two more Grievous Wounds. Four stacks now. Eighty damage per turn in blood loss.

The Matriarch bled out looking at the woman with the singing weapon and the brown eyes that said *I've been waiting for this my entire life*.

Victory Rush. Full heal.

Taryn standing in the valley. Sixteen dead wolves. A warg at her feet. 97 out of 97. Untouched.

"I'm not practicing."

---

### Hadley's Office

---

The clone sits next to Taryn during the briefing. Nods at the right moments.

Sixteen pelts on the floor. Warg skin unrolled like a black carpet. Warg teeth on the desk.

Hadley looks at the woman who was a gate guard four days ago.

"You did this today."

"Took about six minutes, ma'am."

Eighty gold for the wolves. Twenty for the warg. Then the letter. Hadley's seal. Taryn's name.

Letter of commission. Authority to present Ashenveil intelligence to the Coalition Council. Scouting bounty — four seventy-five now, five thousand pending. All in Taryn's name.

Taryn looks at the letter. Looks at the clone she thinks is me.

"You gave it to me. All of it. The credit. The gold. The career."

The clone nods.

---

### The Cold Hand

---

Main street. Walking to the Broken Wheel. Taryn reaches for the clone's hand.

Cold. No pulse. No warmth.

She stops.

"Your hand is always warm."

She squeezes. The fingers don't squeeze back.

"This isn't you."

She looks at the south gate. The empty road. The dark.

"You're already gone."

---

### The South Road

---

Over the wall. Wind Step. Silent. The Windstrider boots on the south road. Stars above. First frost on the grass.

The iron key hums in the storage ring. The ley tether pulls south-southwest. Something waiting. Something sealed. Something the rings were holding back.

Behind me — Millhaven's lanterns getting smaller. A forge glow. Warm windows. A woman in mythril half-plate standing in the street holding a letter of commission and a handful of cold air.

The Still Night is twenty-one days away. Wynn told me about it over stew. The holiday about family and warmth and saying the things you've been carrying.

I don't have family. I don't have a home. I have an iron key pulling south and a road I've never walked and a bag with a stolen chest inside it.

The key pulls. I walk.

---

End of Fraying Empire — Chapter Five: *The Eastbound Run*

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter Six: *The Southern Marker*

### Ashmere 24-25, 1247 AR — The Terminus & Thornkeep

---

The key pulls. I walk.

Millhaven disappears behind me in the dark. Taryn's cold hand on the clone's shoulder is already a memory — the real me is invisible on the south road, Wind-Stepping through bare oaks at 25 miles an hour. The smoke clone takes the main road north, wandering, a decoy for anyone watching. Nobody's watching.

An hour south-southwest. The ley tether sings through the soil under my boots. Living Ground reads the line like a vein — warm, deep, old. Pre-kingdom containment engineers put this seal here two centuries ago and the lock has been waiting for the key I'm carrying ever since.

The terminus. Grid H-9. The edge of the death-binder's thirty-two-mile perimeter. I poke the iron key into the dirt at the ley tether's endpoint. It sinks smoothly to the crossguard.

Bond-Form Sight reads a two-century lock answering.

Living Ground reads forty feet of blood-warm soil spreading from the key.

The death-binder's nearest perimeter node twitches. The system knows something happened — a finger pressing on a wire. The face on the other end is a question for later.

Seal unlock: eight minutes.

---

### The Death Knight's Camp

---

A fire that gives no warmth. A stone ring. A log seat. Black plate armor polished to a mirror finish. The death knight sits with Oathbreaker across his knees. Green fire behind the visor. He doesn't blink because he can't.

A woman is here. Canvas sack. Waterskin. On foot, alone, afraid. She wandered in from the road — the perimeter herded her. The death knight's domain doesn't just ward. It redirects. Anyone walking near the edge gets nudged inward. She didn't find this camp by accident.

She doesn't know that.

"You are the thief," says the death knight.

I toss him the chest. It lands at his armored boots.

"I thought dead men told no tales, yet here we are."

He doesn't flinch. The green fire doesn't shift. Oathbreaker hums — low, metallic, the kind of sound you feel in your teeth.

"Why are you here, swordsman?"

I don't answer. The woman introduces herself — Elda. Looking for her son, Halden, twenty-four, was traveling south from Ashenmere to meet her at the crossroads three days ago. He never arrived. She's been searching since.

I tell the death knight his mother taught him no manners. There's an elderly woman on the road alone and afraid.

"You're elderly, over thirty, right ma'am?"

Elda gives me a look that could curdle milk. "I'm fifty-three, you horrible young man."

I look at the death knight. I look at her. I hold out my hand.

"Kenji."

I grab her hand and walk.

---

### The South Road

---

Behind us, the seal opens. Living Ground reads it — a two-century lock exhaling for the first time. The ground sighs. Warm pulse through the soil, spreading, fading. Whatever's down there is accessible now.

I left the key in the ground.

The death knight watched me leave. He has his chest. He has his questions. He has a seal that just opened at the edge of his lady's domain.

That's his problem.

---

The walk is dark. Cold. Half-moon overhead. Elda doesn't let go of my hand. Fifteen minutes in, she's walking closer. Thirty minutes, she loses the thread of her own sentences. An hour, she asks to stop. Just for a moment.

I don't stop.

She doesn't pull away.

---

Hour two. The oaks close in. Living Ground reads four cold spots — no heartbeat, no warmth, necrotic frost signatures. Arranged in a crescent ahead. The death-binder's perimeter patrol.

Wights. Four of them. Already positioned.

They come from the tree line on both sides. Rusted mail. Grey flesh. Longswords trailing frost vapor. Two in front, two behind. Elda screams. Her hand rips from mine. She stumbles backward — toward the back pair.

They swing on her. She trips on a root and falls under both cuts. The blades gouge dirt where her head was — air where flesh should have been.

The front pair swings on me. The cuts find nothing.

I enter iaido stance.

The draw takes the one standing over Elda — crown to sternum. The Abyssal Shard leaves nothing. The wight unravels in grey dust and rust flakes. Vaporized.

On-kill. The blade carries through. Cuts through the second back wight. Dead. Chains into the third — the counter on the front wight's miss opens it from hip to shoulder. Dead. Chains again — catches the last wight across the torso.

Three hit points left. It staggers.

The nodachi comes down for the kill.

Nat one.

The blade slides wide. A finger's width off.

I don't correct. I don't swing again.

The miss becomes a spin. The nodachi arcs out in a slow deliberate circle — wrist rotating, blade catching moonlight — and I step back. One. Two. The blade floats up over my right shoulder, traces a silver line through the dark, and slides into the scabbard.

*Shhhhiiiing. Click.*

I freeze. Left hand on the scabbard mouth. Right hand open at my side. Weight on the back foot. Eyes on the wight.

Still.

The wight swings at a man who just put his sword away. The longsword passes six inches in front of my chin. Frost vapor brushes the mask.

Miss.

The counter is a draw. The nodachi leaves the scabbard faster than it entered — a rising cut, hip to shoulder. Iaido. Auto-crit.

The last wight comes apart.

I hold the follow-through for one breath. Chiburi flick. Slow sheathe.

*Click.*

Four wights. Two vaporized. Two cut down. The road is dust and rust and silence.

Elda is on the ground staring at me.

"You... what *are* you?"

---

### Wind Step to Thornkeep

---

I hold my hand out. She takes it.

"It's getting late. Dark. I need you to climb on my back. I can get us to the inn quicker."

She doesn't argue. Arms around my shoulders. Canvas sack between us. Her face near my neck. She's very warm for a woman who's been shaking all night.

The ground leaves.

She makes a sound between a scream and a prayer. We're running — not on the road, above it. Oak branches, air-hops, thirty meters between touchpoints. The forest blurs. The moon slides sideways. Twenty minutes. Eight miles. The trees thin. Torchlight ahead.

Thornkeep. Palisade wall. Gate with two lanterns. Garrison flag.

I drop to the road fifty yards out. Walking pace. She's still on my back. Her grip hasn't loosened.

"You can get down now."

A long pause.

"Right."

---

### The Waystation

---

The inn is stone and timber on the main street. Two rooms. A late meal. One gold, three silver. The innkeeper hands over two keys without comment.

The stew is hot. Root vegetables and something that might be mutton. Elda sits across from me. She eats. She doesn't talk. Her eyes keep drifting to my mask, my jaw, the strip of skin between fabric edges. She catches herself. Does it again.

When the bowls are empty, I stand.

"Your room's the second one. Door locks from inside."

She holds the key in both hands. Opens her mouth. Closes it.

"Thank you," she says. "For the road. For the... all of it."

She goes upstairs. The lock turns.

I go to my room. Bare walls. Bed. Window facing the street. Moonlight through the shutters. I set the nodachi against the wall, pull the mask down, and sit on the edge of the bed.

Quiet night. Garrison boots on cobblestones every half hour. The fire downstairs dies to coals.

The seal is open fifteen miles north. The key is in the ground. The death knight watched me walk away. A woman I don't know is on the other side of a wall unable to sleep for reasons she can't name. Her son is somewhere on the south road between Ashenmere and the crossroads. Three days lost.

I left threads behind tonight. The seal. The key. The death knight's questions. Whatever is under that terminus.

But the boy matters more than the lock.

I sleep.

---

*Ashmere 25. Fieldday. Thornkeep Waystation. Morning light through the shutters.*

*The inn smells like breakfast. The road south goes to the border. The garrison goes about its business. Somewhere on the south road, a young man is three days lost.*

*The seal can wait. The death knight can wait. The key is in the ground.*

*The ronin is in a garrison town, and a mother needs her son found.*

---

**Chapter Six — End.**

---

**Chapter Summary:**
- Kenji Wind-Stepped from Millhaven to the iron key terminus (south-southwest, ~1hr)
- Arrived at Sir Corwyn's camp. Returned the stolen iron chest. Death knight asked questions — Kenji never answered.
- Met Elda — untracked NPC, elderly, searching for her son Halden (24, missing 3 days, was traveling south from Ashenmere to meet her at the crossroads). Perimeter redirection herded her to the camp.
- Kenji grabbed Elda's hand and walked away from the death knight, the chest, and the seal mid-conversation.
- Seal opened behind them. Key left in the ground.
- 4 wights (death-binder's perimeter patrol) ambushed on the south road. Enemy ambush — all 4 destroyed. Showman's Sheathe quirk debut (nat 1 → pose → 4 counters → iaido draw-kill).
- Wind-Stepped Elda to Thornkeep (piggyback, ~20 min).
- Arrived midnight. Two rooms at the Waystation. Quiet night. Long rest.
- EXP: +2,800 (4 wights CR 3). Total: 2,212,600 / 2,500,000.
- Irresistible Presence: Elda Stack 1→6 over 2 hours of contact, faded to ~5 overnight.
- Open threads: seal contents unexplored, key unrecovered, death knight aware, Elda's missing son Halden, Thornkeep garrison.

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter Seven: *The Dead Road*

### Thornkeep Waystation — Morning

---

I check on her.

The door opens halfway. She hasn't slept. Red-rimmed eyes, grey hair loose, the room behind her barely touched. The candle burned to a stub. She looks up and everything she spent seven hours building collapses — her shoulders drop, her hand tightens on the doorframe, her eyes find my neck and stay there.

She fights it. Jaw tight. Staring at the wall like it owes her something.

"Did you need something?"

Let's go. I'm taking her to the captain.

---

### Thornkeep Garrison

---

Commander Renna Bracken. Mid-forties. Dark brown hair threaded with grey, pulled back in a soldier's knot. A scar from ear to jaw. Practical steel under a coalition tabard, dented at the shoulder. Cold mug. Colder eyes. She reads the room in two seconds flat.

"Come in. Sit."

Elda sits. The portrait comes out. Halden. Twenty-four. Sandy hair. Kind face. South road from Ashenmere. Three days.

Bracken pulls a map off the wall. Her finger traces the route and stops on a twelve-mile stretch between two jurisdictions.

"There's a twelve-mile gap in the middle where nobody's watching."

She offers Jostin — her best scout, due back from patrol at midday. Fourteen soldiers. Thirty miles of border. No bodies to spare for a search party.

I tell her I fought four wights on the south road last night. That they were after my sexy grandma.

Bracken doesn't blink. She checks her logbook. Jostin logged two sightings this week. I killed four in one night. On foot. With a civilian.

"Where exactly on the south road?"

I let Elda handle the details. Any information that leads to her son is appreciated.

Bracken asks my name. I'm already moving.

---

### The South Road

---

Hop on. Max speed.

Elda's arms lock around my neck. Her face buries against my shoulder. Her pulse hammers through the fabric. Cloud-step, tree-kick, branch-launch. The road blurs.

Twenty minutes south. God Sight catches it first — four undead off the road, rusted mail, cold-fire signatures. They haven't seen me.

I set Elda down behind a fallen log.

"Gotta keep the roads safe. I'll be right back."

---

### Combat — South Road Patrol

**Enemies:** 2 Wights (45 HP, AC 14), 2 Skeleton Warriors (26 HP, AC 16)
**Advantage:** Player (stealth approach, enemies unaware)

The draw comes from nothing.

Wight A doesn't exist anymore. The Abyssal Shard catches it mid-step and the thing unravels — grey dust, rust flakes, a puff of cold air. Vaporized. One hundred and one damage. Gone.

The blade doesn't stop. On-kill momentum into Wight B — horizontal slash through the ribcage. Sixty-four damage. Dead before it registers.

The skeleton warriors turn. I swing on the nearest one — blade clips a raised shield edge. Miss.

Showman's Sheathe.

The nodachi twirls in a slow reverse arc. Tip into the scabbard. *Shhhhiiiing.* Left foot plants. Right hand on the guard. Freeze.

Skeleton Warrior A swings. A six against AC 19. Misses by a yard.

The pose breaks. Iaido draw-strike from the sheathe — guaranteed crit. Ninety-two damage. The bones scatter.

Skeleton Warrior B gets lucky — comes in low, catches me across the ribs. Seven damage. Stings.

My turn. One cut. The last skeleton comes apart at the spine.

Four undead. Two rounds.

**Results:**
- Wight A: VAPORIZED (iaido draw-strike, 101 crit)
- Wight B: DEAD (on-kill continuation, 64 damage)
- Skeleton Warrior A: DEAD (Showman's Sheathe counter, iaido draw-strike, 92 crit)
- Skeleton Warrior B: DEAD (Round 2 attack, 58 damage)
- Kenji: 7 damage taken (326/333 HP)
- EXP: +2,300

---

Elda's voice from behind the log: "Are you *hurt?*"

Naw. Just emotional damage of being separated from you. Hop back on.

---

### Finding Jostin

---

Jostin. Renna Bracken's best scout. Late twenties. Lean. Dark circles under his eyes. Scout's kit, short bow, a journal tucked into his belt.

I give him the details. Missing son. South road. Three days.

He checks his journal. Didn't see a solo traveler three days ago. The gap — twelve miles nobody patrols.

"The activity's getting worse. A month ago I'd see tracks once a week. Now it's every patrol. They're not wandering anymore. They're moving with purpose. Formations. Scouting patterns. I put it in my reports and Commander Bracken puts it in hers and it goes up the chain and nothing comes back down."

He'll search the gap today. If Halden's out there, he'll find sign.

I'm not waiting.

---

### The Gap — Soul Nexus Active

---

Living Ground. Amaris's gift. Plant tremorsense — 200 feet in every direction through the root network. Every footstep, every heartbeat, every body touching soil.

Trade Warmth. Delia's gift. Live and dead trade routes. The road tells you who walked it and when.

Both active. Both passive. Both invisible.

The road answers immediately.

Trade Warmth reads the stone and dirt beneath my boots and the answer comes back cold. Dead cold. No living feet have touched this stretch in three days or more. No merchants. No travelers. The road hasn't gone quiet — it's gone dark.

This is where Halden disappeared.

Then Living Ground pulses. East. 150 feet off the road. Something alive. Humanoid weight. Weak signal. Curled up and holding still.

I head to the signal. Bring Elda.

---

### The Hollow

---

A lean-to of branches and bark between two fallen oaks. Amateur construction. Desperate.

Underneath it — a young man. Sandy hair. Thin face. Pale. Wide, terrified eyes. A broken branch held out like a weapon.

He looks exactly like the portrait.

Three days hiding in this hole. Lips cracked. Hands shaking. Clothes torn from thorns. He ran from grey things on the road and couldn't find his way back.

Elda sees him over my shoulder. The sound she makes isn't a word.

"*Halden —*"

"*Mom?*"

---

### The Long Watch

---

Emergency tent. Travel canvas, two branches, rope work. Hidden in the hollow. I hand Elda the food and take my post outside.

Twelve hours. Living Ground sweeps 200 feet in every direction. Trade Warmth reads the dead road fifty feet west. Hearthsense keeps the tent warm without a fire. No light. No smoke.

Nothing comes.

Inside, Elda feeds her son. Holds him. Talks to him in the voice mothers use when they're holding something together. He sleeps. Wakes. Cries. Sleeps again.

The gap is quiet.

---

### Night

---

I pull the tent flap back. Halden is asleep. Real sleep. Color in his face.

Elda is awake. She looks up and her whole body tenses. Her hands grip her knees. Her eyes go to my face, my neck, the strip of skin above my collar.

"You saved my son."

I walk up to her slowly. Hand on her waist, looking in her eyes. Slowly up — midsection, arms, shoulder. I pull her in.

She breaks. Arms around me, face against my chest, holding on like letting go will kill her. Crying. Breathing me in. She knows what she's doing and she can't stop.

"I don't know what's wrong with me."

I wrap the cloth around her eyes. Gently.

"It'll be alright. Time for you to get some rest. I'll be right behind you."

She lies on her side facing Halden. I lie behind her. The blindfold stays on. The aura has nowhere to go. Her breathing slows. Her hand stays on her son's shoulder. Her back stays against my chest.

She sleeps like she hasn't slept in years.

---

Around 4 AM, a fox noses around the hollow. Four small paws in the tremorsense. It sniffs the canvas. Leaves.

Hearthsense keeps the tent warm. No fire. No light. Three people breathing in a hidden hollow while the dead road sits empty fifty feet west.

---

**Ashmere 26. Stillday. Morning.**

Grey light through the canvas. Frost on the branches. Cold air.

Halden is sleeping. Color back. Breathing steady.

Elda hasn't moved all night.

---

**Chapter Summary:**
- Morning at Thornkeep Waystation. Kenji checked on Elda (IP Stack 5, re-exposure failed, held at 5).
- Took Elda to Commander Renna Bracken at Thornkeep garrison. Reported missing son. Bracken offered Jostin's patrol — 14 soldiers, 30 miles, no spare bodies.
- Wind-Stepped Elda south. Killed 2 wights (1 vaporized) + 2 skeleton warriors on south road. Showman's Sheathe on miss → iaido counter-kill. 7 damage taken.
- Found Corporal Jostin on patrol. Briefed on Halden. Jostin confirmed undead escalation — formations, scouting patterns, reports going up chain with no response.
- Activated Living Ground (Amaris) + Trade Warmth (Delia) through Soul Nexus.
- Wind-Stepped into the 12-mile gap. Trade Warmth: road DEAD, no living traffic 3+ days.
- Living Ground: faint signal 150ft east off-road. Found Halden — 24yo, hiding in lean-to 3 days after fleeing undead.
- Mother-son reunion. Emergency camp. 12-hour guard (no encounters).
- Blindfolded Elda to block IP visual trigger. Spooned her to sleep. 8-hour unguarded rest. Stack 8→7.
- EXP: +2,300 (2 Wights CR 3, 2 Skeleton Warriors CR 2). Total: 2,214,900 / 2,500,000.
- IP: Elda Stack 5→6→7→8→7 over the chapter. Blindfold mechanic discovered.
- Halden: alive, dehydrated, hypothermic, fed and stabilized.
- Open threads: escort Elda+Halden home, south road dead zone, seal contents unexplored, Thornkeep garrison understaffed, Pallid March building, Still Night in 19 days.

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter Eight: *The Cell*
