### The Clone Trick — Morning

---

I wait outside the tent for them to wake.

Grey light. Cold air. Frost on the branches. The hollow is quiet. The dead road sits empty fifty feet west. Living Ground reads nothing.

Elda stirs first. I hear her move inside the canvas — fabric shifting, a breath catching. She'll pull the blindfold.

Smoke bomb. Invisibility. Clone.

The smoke rolls out low and quiet. I'm gone before it clears. The clone materializes — me, but not me. Visual only. No biological signature. No aura. It posts up by the tent entrance, arms crossed, looking cool. The kind of pose you hold for a painting nobody commissioned.

Elda pushes the tent flap open. Blinks in the grey light. Sees the clone.

Her eyes hit his face. His neck. The strip of skin above the collar.

Nothing.

No save. No escalation. The stack holds at seven but doesn't push. The clone is wallpaper. A picture of a man. She looks at it the way you look at a well-made statue — appreciation without the heat.

The blindfold is folded on the ground beside her. She left it there. Didn't need it anymore — didn't know she still does.

I stand three feet away, invisible, and talk. Pitch it toward the clone so it sounds like it's coming from him.

"So want to go home? Think he's good enough to walk?"

---

Halden is awake. Color back. The ankle is wrapped and he's testing weight on it — gingerly, holding the tent pole, wincing. He can hobble — slow, but moving.

Elda watches the clone while she answers. Her voice is steady. The tears from last night are gone. She's a mother with a plan now — get the boy home.

"He can lean on me. We'll manage."

I pull a bag from my pack. A hundred gold. Heavy. I toss it — invisible hand, so it arcs out of nowhere and lands at her feet with a *clink* that doesn't match anything she's seeing.

She jumps. Looks down. Looks at the clone. The clone didn't move.

"Where I'm from, it's a custom to throw money at sexy women." A pause. "Um. Sorry. All I had was coins."

Her face does something complicated. Confusion. Embarrassment. The ghost of a smile she fights down. She picks up the bag. Weighs it. Her eyes go wide.

"This is — this is a *hundred* —"

She looks at the clone. The clone looks cool.

She puts the bag in her traveling sack. Tucks it deep. And then she smiles into the cup she's holding — the small clay travel cup, morning water — and the smile stays there where she thinks nobody can see it.

I see it.

---

"See you later, Elda. You know what to do from here. That patrol from earlier shouldn't be too far — they can get you back to town. If you need me, you know where to find me, beautiful."

She doesn't know where to find me.

The clone does a dramatic crouch. Then runs. Jumps to the nearest tree — full extension, one hand on a branch, swing up. Backflip to a higher branch. Lands in a ninja crouch. Holds it. Then works his way up and north, branch to branch, until the canopy swallows him.

Elda watches the whole thing with her mouth slightly open.

Halden, leaning on the tent pole: "Mom. Who *was* that?"

"I don't know his name."

She's smiling into the cup again.

---

I follow them. Invisible. Real. Twenty feet behind.

They're slow. Halden leans on her shoulder. She takes the weight without complaint. They find the road and follow it north toward Thornkeep. Elda keeps looking at the trees — looking for the man who isn't there. The man who's behind her, not above her.

Jostin's patrol finds them an hour in. Fourteen soldiers, road-worn, professional. Jostin does a double-take at the civilian pair on a closed road. Elda shows him the garrison waystation token from yesterday.

Handoff clean. Jostin assigns two soldiers to escort them the rest of the way. Halden gets a shoulder to lean on that isn't his mother's.

I watch until they're a quarter mile north. Safe.

Then I turn south and follow Jostin.

---

### Shadowing the Patrol

---

Jostin's patrol works the south road like professionals. Tight formation. Scouts forward. Jostin in the center with his journal out, marking terrain, noting tracks. They move with the quiet efficiency of people who do this every day and hate that it's necessary.

I follow from the trees. Invisible. Wind Step between branches. Eating jerky on a high limb, legs swinging, watching them work.

They find the phalanx two hours in.

---

### The Skeleton Phalanx

---

Eight skeletons. Not wanderers — *soldiers*. Shield wall. Interlocking formation. They're standing in the road like they own it, rusted shields overlapping, empty eye sockets facing north. Waiting.

Jostin holds up a fist. The patrol stops. He studies them through a spyglass for a full minute.

"Formation holders. Old stock — battlefield dead, dug up, re-dressed. The shields are Ashenmere garrison surplus from the border war. Twenty years in the ground minimum."

He gives the order. The patrol splits — six soldiers hit the shield wall from the front while four flankers swing wide. Jostin directs from twenty feet back, calling adjustments.

The front line hits. The phalanx holds. Shields lock tighter. The skeletons don't panic, don't scatter, don't break ranks. They absorb the charge and push back as a unit.

One of the flankers gets through. Destroys a skeleton on the left edge. The formation adjusts — the remaining seven close the gap. Seamless.

"That's remote command," Jostin mutters, writing in his journal. "Pre-programmed patrol routes. The formation holds until physically broken."

They break it in four minutes. Methodical. Professional. Not a single soldier down, though two take hits — one shield arm, one thigh. Walking wounds.

I watch the whole thing from a branch. Chewing jerky. Taking notes that don't exist on paper.

When the last skeleton falls, the bones just... stop. No residual animation. No death rattle. The command signal cut and the puppets went slack. Whatever is running these things isn't here. Isn't within a mile.

Jostin collects bone fragments for his report. Marks the location in his journal. The patrol reforms and continues south.

I follow them back to Thornkeep.

---

### Bracken's Office — Invisible

---

Jostin goes straight to Bracken.

Her office. Second floor of the garrison hall. Stone walls, narrow window, a desk covered in dispatches and maps. Commander Renna Bracken sits behind it in practical steel, dented at the shoulder. Forty-four years old. Scar from her right ear to her jaw. Grey-green eyes that could cut glass.

I'm already inside. Sitting in the corner. Invisible. Eating.

Jostin reports. The phalanx. The formation. The remote command structure. Old stock from battlefields. Three escalations in two weeks — lone walkers, then pairs, now drilled formations.

Bracken listens. Doesn't interrupt. When he finishes, she pulls out paper and starts writing.

Three letters.

The first to Katya — requesting sixty soldiers and one combat mage. The second to Vess — requesting a Coalition-level response timeline. The third to the Ashenmere garrison — asking what they're seeing on their side, courier only, she doesn't trust whisper stone relays.

"That's three dispatches in four months that say the same thing," she says. "Requesting reinforcement. Confirmed escalation. Forty-two soldiers against whatever is organizing these things. If I don't get a response to this round, I'm pulling the garrison back to the waystation perimeter and letting the south road go."

Jostin nods. He looks like he hasn't slept in weeks because he hasn't slept in weeks.

"Dismissed."

He leaves. Door closes.

Bracken stares at the dispatches. Alone in her office. Except she isn't alone.

I drop visibility. Sitting in her chair — the guest chair across from the desk. Visible. Munching on food. Staring at her.

---

Her sword is out before the jerky clears my teeth.

The blade kisses my throat. Fast. Professional. Twenty-six years of muscle memory in the draw.

"Who are you. How did you get in here. Start talking or start bleeding."

Her grey-green eyes are locked on my mask. She's not shaking. She's not scared. She's a woman who held a bridge with twelve soldiers against a cavalry charge and the scar on her jaw proves it.

I stare at her. Take in everything. Not the soldier — the woman. Five-eight, five-nine. Lean. Narrow waist under the leather armor. Modest chest. Strong legs. The grey-threaded hair in the soldier's knot shows the line of her neck. High cheekbones. The scar from ear to chin should be ugly. It isn't. It draws the eye to her face instead of away.

She's not beautiful the way Elda is. She's the kind of woman who looks better the longer you stare.

She can tell I'm staring.

"I'm here to help you, old lady. Elda's been reunited with her son, so now I'm here with you. And from what I'm seeing — you need some help." I glance at the sword. "Also, can you please get your stick out of my face? It's touching my throat and I think it's going to make me gag at this rate."

---

"Elda. The herbalist. And Halden, broken ankle. They were on the missing roster from the south road. Three days overdue." Her grip shifts on the sword. "Where are they."

"And I'm *forty-four*, you little shit. Not elderly."

The sword drops two inches. Still pointed at me. But she's listening.

"Start with your name. Then tell me how you found two missing civilians and walked through my garrison like an open market — and then I'll decide whether you get a cell or a conversation."

---

### The Gamble

---

I'm here for you specifically, actually. But before I ask a favor — do you like to gamble?

I lay out the terms. Duel. If I win, I get her for three days — she puts someone else in charge and comes with me. If she wins, I give her my name, the intel on the skeleton in the mist, and I enlist under her command.

"No."

She doesn't bend. Forty-two people. Closed road. Organized undead. Four months of unanswered letters. She's not gambling her post.

Fine.

"Well then I guess you're going to have to arrest me. From this point on I'm not talking until you accept my gamble. But I'll follow any physical instructions you give."

I shut up. The bit starts.

---

### The Cell

---

Converted storeroom. Iron-banded door, solid wood, no viewing slot. Barred window near the ceiling. Bench bolted to the wall. Bucket in the corner. Smells like old grain and damp stone.

They never ask for my weapons.

I sit. Chew jerky. The bit is the bit.

---

Forty-five minutes. The door opens.

Bracken. Outer armor off. Fitted linen shirt, belted at the waist, sleeves pushed to elbows. Sword on hip. She tells herself it's because the office was warm.

She drags a stool in. Sits across from me. The cell door stays open behind her.

"No swords, no guards, no rank. Just two people in a room."

She leans forward. Elbows on knees. Forearms bare — old training scars, campaign marks.

"I'm not gambling my post. But a cell isn't going to stop you and we both know it. So tell me what you actually want."

I stare her in the eye. "I think I already told you. I'm here to help you, old lady. You wanted to get me alone in a cell first for some reason, so... here we are. We really should do something about that undead, though. Let me know when you're ready to duel. Have the blacksmith make me a reverse katana so I don't hurt you."

"You're the most arrogant man I've ever met. And I served under General Cedwyn during the Thornwall Offensive, so that is a *high* bar."

She crosses her arms. "If I duel you — *if* — and you win. Three days. What exactly do you think happens in three days?"

We solve the undead problem. If you win, I'll join your army as a resource... to use... anyway you like, love.

Her ears go red.

She asks what happens if she just asks me to help. Because people are dying and I clearly can.

"Who *are* you?"

Softer than anything she's said since I met her.

---

### The Duel

---

I sit on the stool. Lean back. Arms crossed.

"Hmm, you're right. People are dying. Belay that last order, no reverse katana."

I walk my nodachi to the corner. Set it against the wall. Turn back. Crack my knuckles.

"I'll use my hands. Fight like your life depends on it — you can use your real sword. If I die, I have a letter on me with enemy intelligence that'll still help you win."

I don't have a letter.

"Come at me, toots."

She draws.

---

My body drops into something I've never been taught. Left foot forward, right heel raised, hands up — lead hand open and low, rear hand guarding the chin. Weight centered but mobile. It's not from this world. A muscle memory from before.

"*Hwaaaaaaaa.*"

She blinks.

The jab catches her on the nose. Palm strike. Straight line, no wind-up. Her head snaps back. Eyes water.

The kick folds her. Side kick to the solar plexus. She hits the far wall with her shoulder blades and slides down to one knee. Sword still in hand. Twenty-six years of *never let go*.

I hop on one leg. Jab the air. Swipe my thumb across my nose. Spit on the stone.

"You call this a fight, Captain? You must become like *waaaaaater*... and not be rigid like stone."

She adapts. Stops lunging. Goes defensive. Sword level, eyes on my hips. Waiting for the counter.

"I'm a *commander*, not a captain. And I've fought things faster than you."

She hasn't.

---

I take the top of the hakama off. Drop the hat. Drop the mask. Purple hair falls to my back and shoulders.

She sees me. All of me — the man behind the ronin and the mask. The face that has broken eighteen women across four books.

Her sword drops three inches.

I drop into a full split on the stone floor. Punching air. Casual. Hand on chin. Looking up at her midsection.

"I see, Captain... you are afraid. It is good to fear death. Or is it something else you fear?" I study her like a painting. "I wonder what you look like under that armor."

"You are *in the middle of a duel*." Her voice cracks. "Stand up."

---

Leg sweep from the split. She goes down. I take her boots before she can process what happened. Then the cuirass. Belt. Everything that isn't the linen shirt goes in the corner with the swords.

"People are dying. You really should take this seriously."

I wave an old piece of mail from my pack like it's battle plans. It's a receipt from Pip's inn.

---

She's on her back. Barefoot. Hair down. Looking up at me.

"Are you not going to fight, grandma? The strange man said he had enemy intel and he has your boots."

Something snaps.

She comes up swinging. The best swing of the fight — angry, technical, real. The longsword catches my left forearm. Thin line of blood. First blood. Mine.

I don't flinch.

She stands over me, breathing hard, sword extended, barefoot, hair in her face. She sees the cut. She sees it barely bleeding. She sees the muscle underneath.

"Who *are* you?"

---

I drop the boots. Roll backward.

"Hmm, I said fight like your life depends on it."

I sit on the stool. Arms crossed.

"But if you really want to yield, I'll give you an advantage. A different battle. Whoever makes the other finish five times first wins. Take off your clothes to let me know you consent. You don't consent — I accept your yield, duel's over, and I'm going to enjoy the help around my garden for three days."

---

The silence is absolute.

She walks to the door. Barefoot on cold stone. Each step deliberate.

The door closes. The latch clicks.

She turns around.

"If a single word leaves this cell — I don't care what you are, how fast you are, or how pretty your hair is. I will make the Thornwall Offensive look like a *garden party*."

The shirt comes off.

---

### Fade to Black

---

I walk up slow. Hand on her chin. Kiss her. And I channel — Creation energy, raw, unfiltered, pouring through the contact. The split lip seals. The bruise fades. The scar from her ear to her jaw — twenty years old, healed white — smooths and vanishes. The slash across her ribs. The puncture on her shoulder. Every mark the border put on her, erased in a kiss.

Her fingers find her jaw. Feel smooth skin. She trembles.

Then I pick her up.

---

The wall cracks. Floor to ceiling.

---

She pins me. Fifteen minutes. The stool breaks. The bench bolts groan. Lover's Vigor transmits on the first contact — her eyes shift, grey-green brightening with a golden ring around the pupils. +50% to all stats. She feels it hit like a second wind that doesn't stop.

She rides like she fights. Relentless. Tactical. She finds what works and stays there.

---

The cell bars bend. Two of them bow outward three inches. Stone dust showers from the ceiling anchor points. Creation energy heals every mark on her shoulders the moment it forms.

---

She's winning. 4-2.

I fall back. Drained. On the stone floor. For the first time since Book 1, I've been in a fight I'm actually losing.

She looks at me. Something clicks behind those Vigor-gold eyes. The same thing that clicked when she held the bridge with twelve soldiers.

She punches me in the jaw.

Vigor-buffed. Hits like a mace. Before I can recover she's on me — determined, furious, a woman who hasn't won anything in four months and is going to win *this*.

Then — before losing it herself — she forces herself up. The discipline is written across her whole body. She drops to her knees. One hand on my throat. The other where it needs to be. Her mouth finishes the job.

5-3. Bracken.

---

She sits back on the cold stone. Wipes her mouth with the back of her hand. The same gesture she used for the blood from her split lip an hour ago.

The cell is destroyed. Crack in the wall floor to ceiling. Two bars bent outward. The stool is kindling. The bench bolts half-pulled from stone. The door hanging crooked on its hinges.

She looks at the damage. Looks at me. Flat on my back. Purple hair on the floor.

"I win."

A pause.

"Now tell me your name. And tell me about the undead."

---

**Chapter Summary:**
- Morning: Clone trick for Elda (100GP gift, IP bypass — clone has no biological aura). Escort handoff to Jostin's patrol.
- Shadowed Jostin's patrol invisibly. Witnessed skeleton phalanx engagement (8 skeletons, shield wall, remote command, old battlefield stock). Patrol won in 4 minutes. Two walking wounded.
- Spied on Bracken's classified briefing. Garrison at 35% (42/120). Three escalations in 2 weeks. Three letters dispatched: Katya (60 soldiers + mage), Vess (response timeline), Ashenmere garrison (cross-check). 4 months of ignored requests.
- Appeared visible in Bracken's office. Sword at throat. Proposed duel: win = 3 days her assistance, lose = enlist under her command.
- Refused. Arrested voluntarily. Came to cell 45 min later.
- Unarmed JKD duel. Kenji dominated physically — jab, sweep, stripped armor, kick after yield.
- Transitioned to intimate contest (5-finish race). Lover's Vigor transmitted after first round. Bracken won 5-3 on determination and Vigor-buffed stamina.
- Creation energy healed all scars (jaw, ribs, shoulder). Cell destroyed (cracked wall, bent bars, broken stool, warped door).
- Kenji owes: his name, undead intel, and service under Bracken's command.
- Renna Bracken: 18th intimate partner. IP Stack 5+ (Obsessed). Lover's Vigor active (golden eyes, +50% all stats, 5 days).

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter Nine: *The Name*

### The Cell — Aftermath

---

"Kenji."

He falls back. Eyes rolling. Hits the stone floor like a sack of grain. Naked. Purple hair fanned out across the cold stone. Snoring within three seconds.

He gave her his name. One word, half-conscious, falling asleep. Terms satisfied. Technically.

---

Bracken stares down at him.

"Kenji," she repeats. Quietly. To herself. Filing it somewhere deep.

Then the soldier takes over. She grabs the linen shirt. Pulls it on. Grabs the cuirass from the corner — laces the left side, starts the right—

**BANG.**

The crooked door slams open. Three garrison soldiers pile in — swords drawn, shields up, formation tight. Two more in the corridor with crossbows leveled. The young guard from earlier is shouting something about structural damage and possible siege equipment.

"COMMANDER, WE HEARD—"

They stop.

The cell looks like a trebuchet round went through it. Crack in the wall floor to ceiling. Two iron bars bent outward like something tried to claw its way out. The stool is splinters. The bench is half-ripped from the floor. Stone dust everywhere. The door frame is warped.

And in the middle of it — a naked man with purple hair, spread-eagle on the floor, snoring peacefully. Smiling in his sleep.

And their commander. One strap away from dressed. Hair wild. Flushed from her collarbones to her ears. A bruise forming on her jaw — from a fist, not a weapon. And her eyes — grey-green with a gold ring around the pupils that wasn't there this morning.

The lead soldier — a sergeant, older, seen some things — takes this in. All of it. His eyes go from the naked man. To the commander. To the wall crack. To the bent bars. Back to the naked man. Back to the commander's one loose armor strap.

His mouth opens.

Closes.

Opens.

"...Ma'am?"

Bracken finishes the strap. Pulls it tight. Snaps the buckle. Runs her fingers through her hair — a gesture so far from military regulation it might as well be a signed confession — and straightens up. Full commander posture. Spine like a pike handle.

"The prisoner resisted interrogation. The cell sustained structural damage. You're looking at the result."

The sergeant looks at the crack in the wall. Looks at the bent iron bars. Looks at the sleeping naked man who weighs maybe a hundred and eighty pounds.

"He... did this, ma'am?"

"Did I stutter, Sergeant?"

"No ma'am."

The young guard from earlier is craning his neck over the sergeant's shoulder. His eyes are the size of dinner plates. He is going to tell everyone about this.

"You." Bracken points at the young guard. Her voice could freeze a river. "If I hear one word — one syllable — in the mess hall, the barracks, or anywhere else in my garrison, I will have you digging latrines until your grandchildren feel the blisters. Am I understood?"

"Yes ma'am."

"Get a blanket for the prisoner. He's staying in this cell tonight." She steps over Kenji's legs on her way to the door. Doesn't look down. "Nobody enters without my authorization. Nobody speaks to him. Nobody looks at him."

She pauses in the doorway. The sergeant is staring at the gold ring in her eyes. She knows he noticed. She can't do anything about it.

"Dismissed."

She walks out. Measured steps. Straight back. Not a hair out of place — except all of it.

The soldiers file out. The sergeant is last. He takes one more look at the crack in the wall, the bent bars, and the unconscious purple-haired man on the floor who is smiling in his sleep.

He closes the broken door. It doesn't latch. It sort of leans against the frame.

From the corridor, barely a whisper: "What in the actual—"

"**Sergeant.**"

"Moving, ma'am."

---

Kenji sleeps. The broken cell holds the cold and the quiet and the faint smell of mint salve. Somewhere above, Commander Renna Bracken sits at her desk with new eyes and no scar and writes the word *Kenji* on a scrap of paper, stares at it for thirty seconds, and burns it in the candle.

---

### The March South

---

He woke two hours later. Put on his gear. Waited in the cell.

---

### The Debrief

---

The door opened wrong — scraped against the warped frame where it didn't fit anymore. Bracken stood in the corridor. Full armor, every strap buckled, hair retied in the soldier's knot. Commander posture locked back in place like a door bolted shut. The only thing different was the eyes — grey-green with a gold ring that caught the torchlight.

She didn't comment on it.

"Walk with me."

---

Her office. Same desk. Same dispatches. Same narrow window. She sat. He sat across from her — the guest chair. Same chair he'd been eating jerky in when she put a sword to his throat.

"Start with the undead."

He told her. All of it. The dead zone south. The mist line at five miles. Skeleton sentries posted in pairs at two-mile intervals — not wandering, not random. *Posted.* Like soldiers on watch. Remote command running them from somewhere further south.

Bracken's pen stopped on the dispatch paper. "Remote command. You're telling me they're receiving *orders.*"

"From something smart enough to run formations. That phalanx your patrol hit this morning — eight skeletons in a shield wall. They adjusted when one went down. Closed the gap. That's not instinct. That's tactical command."

She wrote. Didn't look up. "What else."

---

The death knight.

"Sir Corwyn the Fallen. Camps at the terminus site — stone ring, log seat, black plate polished like he's expecting inspection. He's not mindless. He talks. He has *opinions.* And he's posted eighty yards from an iron seal that I opened."

Bracken's pen stopped again. "You opened a seal."

"With a key I found in a Pre-Kingdom ruin north of Millhaven."

"What's under the seal?"

"Don't know. Walked away before I looked."

The pen didn't move. She stared at him.

"You opened an ancient seal in a dead zone eighty yards from a death knight and then *walked away without looking.*"

"I had a woman and her kid to get home. Priorities."

---

He pulled the nodachi from across his back. Set it on the desk between them — red-black steel, faint internal luminescence. The blade was longer than her sword by a foot. It hummed on the wood.

"Corwyn's wearing full plate. Heavy. Old paladin kit. He'll resist bleed effects — the man's already dead, he's not going to hemorrhage. But this—" He tapped the blade. "Twenty-five percent chance to vaporize what it crits. Abyssal annihilation. If you send someone at him with a regular sword, they'll chip steel for an hour. With this, one good hit and he's *gone.*"

Bracken looked at the nodachi. Then at him.

"You're lending me your weapon."

"I'm giving you an option. He's your problem. Your people. If I'm south hunting the command source, someone needs to handle the knight at the terminus."

She picked up the blade. Heavier than she expected — she adjusted her grip, tested the balance. Vigor-buffed strength made it manageable. The steel hummed against her palm.

She set it back down. Didn't push it away.

---

"Don't worry, beautiful. I won't let your people come to harm. I'm good at fighting. But—"

He stopped.

"I've never been good at puzzles. I can't—" A pause. Longer than it should have been. "I can't read."

The office went quiet.

Bracken looked at him. Really looked. A different look than the one she'd had in the cell — clear of the aura, clear of the gold-edge sharpness in her vision. She looked at him the way a commander looks at a resource she's assessing for deployment.

"You can't read."

"Maps, signs, letters — none of it. Numbers I can do. Words, no."

"How long?"

"Always."

---

She stood. Walked to the window. Looked out at the garrison yard — soldiers drilling, the sound of steel, the routine that held forty-two people together on a border nobody cared about.

"Jostin."

"Ma'am?"

She'd already sent for him. The door opened and the scout walked in — journal in hand, circles under his eyes, the posture of a man who expected more bad news.

"You're going south with him." She nodded at the ronin. "Deep assault. Past the mist line. Find the command source and destroy it."

Jostin looked at the masked man in the guest chair. The same man who'd been invisible in the trees above his patrol that morning.

"He's your brain," Bracken said. "He reads terrain, keeps notes, thinks tactically. Everything you can't do — he does."

The ronin didn't argue.

"Brynn. Shield infantry. Level-headed, quiet, follows orders. She'll keep Jostin alive while you do what you do."

"Three-person team?"

"Three-person team. You lead. Jostin scouts. Brynn holds. I need the command source dead before it sends anything else north."

---

He stood. Headed for the door.

"Thanks, Commander. You'd make a great mom. I appreciate you for considering babysitting me."

Bracken's hand went to the desk. Both palms flat. She didn't move for three full seconds. The comment landed somewhere she wasn't braced — under the armor, under the rank, in the place where a woman who'd held a border alone for four months heard someone say *you'd take care of me* and didn't know what to do with it.

"Get out of my office."

He got.

Her hand stayed on the desk after the door closed. The gold ring in her eyes caught the window light.

---

### The March South

---

The south road at night was a different animal.

Jostin took point. Journal out, short bow across his back, moving through the dark with the quiet competence of a man who'd done this route a hundred times. Brynn walked shield-right — heavy steel angled to cover, sword drawn, eyes scanning the tree line without breaking stride.

The first skeleton sentry pair appeared at mile one. Two figures standing in the road, rusted shortswords, empty eye sockets pointed south. They turned when the party approached. Both skulls locked onto the ronin. Only the ronin.

"They're tracking you," Jostin said quietly. "Just you. We're invisible to them."

The ronin walked through. The skeletons watched him pass and resumed pointing south.

Mile two. Another pair. Same behavior. South-pointing, Kenji-tracking, teammate-ignoring.

Mile three. Mile four. The pattern held. Eight skeletons on four posts, all locked on one man, all pointing the same direction.

"That's a lure," Jostin said, writing without slowing. "They want you going south."

---

At mile five, the mist came.

Living Ground contracted — 200 feet to 150, to 120, to 80. Something ahead was drinking the ley network. God Sight dropped to 40 feet. The stars disappeared behind a canopy of dead branches and thickening vapor.

Two points of blue fire watched from seventy feet ahead. Wights. Heavier than skeletons. Armored. Flanking a stone threshold half-buried in dead brush.

"You're going to walk straight at them," Jostin said.

Not a question.

The ronin drew.

The first wight didn't see the blade. The iaido strike bisected it from collarbone to hip — 111 points of force through corroded mail and grey bone. The pieces hit the ground and crumbled to ash.

The second wight lunged. Two cuts. The first caught it across the midsection. The second took its head. Both halves collapsed into rust and silence.

Three seconds.

"I want you to know I'm writing that down," Jostin said, "and I don't expect anyone to believe it."

---

The ronin didn't enter the structure. He went *around* it.

Wind Step kicked off dead earth and he circled the perimeter — three skeleton pairs at cardinal points, one wight on the far side. Six iaido draws, six sheathes, six measured *clicks* of steel on lacquered wood. The wight at the back saw him coming and had half a second to raise its longsword before the guaranteed crit went through its midsection.

Seven kills. Zero damage. Forty seconds.

He Wind Stepped back to the road and cleared every sentry pair between mile five and mile one. Eight more skeletons. Four more draw-strikes. Four more vaporizations of bone and rust into ash that the mist swallowed before it touched the ground.

Five miles of empty road behind him. Five miles of nothing standing.

---

### The Node

---

The structure was one room. Pre-Kingdom architecture — fitted stone blocks, no mortar, ancient precision. And at its center: a relay stone. Black basalt, waist height, with channels carved in patterns that pulsed with bruise-colored necromantic light. Bone-ceramic lining — the same material the Pallid March border markers were made from.

"That's a sending post," Jostin said. "Break it and the local network goes dark. But the source will know."

The ronin drew.

The first strike cracked the stone — 70 points through enchanted basalt. The channels screamed. Then the stored necromantic energy backlashed outward in a wave of cold. The ronin shrugged it off. Jostin and Brynn did not — both staggered, both took the hit, both stayed on their feet.

The second strike unmade it. The stone split into six pieces. The bone-ceramic shattered to powder. The bruise-light died.

And Living Ground *bloomed*. Eighty feet to a hundred. To a hundred and twenty. The suppression field collapsed. The ley network started breathing again.

A symbol was scratched into the wall beside the doorway. A circle with a vertical line through it. Recent. Something with hands and intelligence had marked this place.

---

### Node Two — The Perimeter

---

Mile seven and a half. Jostin's maps had it marked from three weeks ago. Twelve skeletons in the sentry ring then. Twelve now — plus two wights.

"I had 'walks straight at them' written down," Jostin said, looking at the first node's aftermath. "I was wrong."

He was wrong about the second node too. The ronin circled again. Counterclockwise. Six skeleton pairs. Each one: draw, kill, chain-kill, sheathe, cloud-step to the next. The two wights dropped to iaido strikes — one overkill, one vaporized.

Fourteen kills. Zero damage. The perimeter was clean.

Jostin counted the sheathe-clicks from the high ground. Reconstructed the entire sweep route from sound alone.

"You circle counterclockwise. Every time." He tapped his journal. "If I can figure that out in two nodes, something smarter than me can figure it out in three."

---

The second node was different. Stairs going down. Underground. The relay stone pulsing below ground level.

But the ronin held back.

"Wait here guys," he said. "Going to take out the sentries behind us."

He Wind Stepped north. The road between miles five and seven had fresh sentries — two pairs posted since the march through. The command source had *restocked.* But miles one through five were also occupied again. Four pairs where there should have been ash and silence. New bone. New rust. Reposted within hours.

Four pairs. Eight skeletons. Draw, kill, chain, sheathe, sprint. The road was empty for the second time tonight.

He came back.

"Road clear?"

"Yep."

Jostin wrote something in his journal and didn't show anyone.

---

### Camp

---

The creek bed was forty yards from the node entrance. Brynn set up a fire — hidden, professional, barely visible from ten feet away. She cooked.

The ronin looked at Jostin.

"Yo... *psssst*... between me and you, be honest... how much junk is Brynn carrying back there? One out of five? I mean... if you were a baker, would you consider that cake to be multi-layered?"

Jostin's pen stopped.

He looked at the ronin. He looked at Brynn. He looked back.

He held up three fingers.

Then immediately put his hand down, opened his journal, and started drawing with intense concentration. His ears were dark red from the collar up.

Brynn turned around with the cleaned pot. She looked at Jostin's red ears. She looked at the ronin.

"What."

Jostin drew a very detailed staircase.

---

The ronin ate. Brynn's food was better than it had any right to be — salted meat, softened root vegetables, something herbal from a pouch on her belt. Garrison winter-patrol cooking. The kind that keeps soldiers alive in the cold.

"You're the best, Brynn. Wish I could take you with me everywhere."

Her hands stopped on the bedroll strap. One second. Two. She pulled it tight with a sharp *snap.*

"Get some sleep, soldier," she said to Jostin — who was already asleep.

She didn't sleep for the first hour.

---

### The Watch

---

The ronin slept six hours. Jostin woke him at three in the morning — field rest protocol, enough sleep for a full long rest with three hours of watch remaining.

He ate. Sat on the creek bed lip with the nodachi across his knees. Let Living Ground sweep in slow circles.

At four-fifteen, a wight appeared at the edge of perception. Single scout. Cautious. Moving north to check on the missing sentries.

He intercepted it a hundred yards from camp. Drew. Vaporized. Walked back. Nobody woke up.

At five in the morning, the relay stone's pulse stopped.

Ten minutes of silence. The hum that had been bleeding through the soil since they arrived — gone. Like a room where the fan turns off. Then it resumed. Same rhythm. Same frequency.

Something upstream had *paused to think.*

---

Pre-dawn. Ashmere 27. Frost on everything. First light bleeding grey through bare branches. Jostin woke. Brynn was already up — rolling her bedroll, shield within arm's reach. She'd barely slept.

"There's food in the pot." A pause. "Sir."

The *sir* was new.

The node entrance waited. Forty yards south. Stairs going down. Relay pulsing.

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter Ten: *The South Road*

### Node 2 — Underground

---

The stairs went down twenty feet into fitted stone. Same Pre-Kingdom architecture — no mortar, ancient precision. The relay stone pulsed at the center of a single chamber. Bruise-colored necromantic light. Bone-ceramic channels carved in patterns that hurt to look at.

Jostin sketched the layout from the doorway. Brynn held the threshold — shield angled to cover the stairs behind them.

The ronin drew.

The first strike cracked the stone. The channels screamed. Stored necromantic energy backlashed outward — the cold wave hit all three of them. Jostin staggered. Brynn took it on the shield and held.

The second strike finished it. The basalt split. The bone-ceramic crumbled. The bruise-light went out.

Living Ground bloomed. The ley network started breathing again.

Circle-and-line symbol on the wall. Same hand. Same tool. Recent.

"That's two," Jostin said, writing. "Same marking at both. Same architecture. Same relay design. This is a network, not random outposts."

---

### The March — Miles 7.5 to 10

---

South. Deeper into the dead zone. The frost thickened as they moved. Temperature hadn't broken freezing. Wouldn't for another hour.

The ronin took point. Jostin behind. Brynn shield-right.

Mile eight. Empty road. The sentries that should have been here were already ash — cleared during the night march.

Mile eight and a half. Living Ground detected the dead zone boundary — the line where healthy soil stopped and drained earth began. The line had moved. South. Two hundred yards south of where it had been before Node 2 fell.

"The boundary's retreating," Jostin said, watching the ronin's head tilt. "As we destroy nodes, the dead zone contracts. The ley network reclaims the soil." He wrote it down. "If we destroy enough of them, the whole zone collapses."

Mile nine. The soil changed again. Deeper corruption. Living Ground degraded — two hundred feet to a hundred and fifty, to a hundred.

Mile nine and a half. Two skeleton sentries. Posted at the road edge. South-pointing. They turned when the ronin approached. Both skulls locked onto him.

He walked through them. Drew. Two cuts. Two kills. Didn't break stride.

"He didn't even slow down," Brynn said.

It was the longest sentence she'd spoken all morning.

---

### Node 3 — The Prepared Position

---

Mile ten. The tree line east of the road. They stopped.

Node 3 was different.

The structure was the same Pre-Kingdom architecture — fitted stone, no mortar, ancient precision. But the garrison around it was *double.* Twenty-one skeletons in three concentric rings of seven. The outer ring faced outward — sentries. The middle ring patrolled a circuit around the node entrance. The inner ring stood shoulder to shoulder at the threshold, shields up, swords drawn. They weren't wandering. They were **garrisoned.**

Five wights. One at each cardinal point of the outer ring, and one at the entrance behind the inner skeleton formation. The entrance wight was bigger than the others — heavier armor, a longsword that still had an edge. It hadn't moved in the twenty minutes they'd been watching.

Jostin closed his journal softly.

"It doubled the garrison. Node 1 had ten. Node 2 had fourteen. This one has twenty-six." He tapped the page. "That's not reinforcement — that's a *prepared position.* Something told them we were coming."

A pause. He glanced at the ronin sideways.

"You're going to circle counterclockwise. Start with the sentries. Work inward. I've seen it twice. The wights at the cardinal points are spaced forty yards apart — if you're fast enough they won't signal each other before you reach the next one."

He waited a beat.

"But you're going to do it anyway, even if I told you not to. So I wrote the fallback in case the inner ring collapses on Brynn and me while you're mid-sweep."

Brynn shifted her shield grip. Her eyes hadn't left the perimeter.

"There's food in the satchel if you want it before." A pause. "Sir."

---

### The Straight Line

---

Jostin opened his mouth.

The ronin was already gone.

No circle. No sweep. No counterclockwise anything. He walked *forward* — straight at the outer ring, nodachi across his back, left foot leading, thumb on the guard.

The first skeleton sentry turned. Rusted shortsword came up—

*Click.*

The draw. The cut. The skeleton bisected at the ribcage and the top half turned to ash before it hit the ground. Vaporized. The bottom half collapsed. The blade didn't stop.

The wight at the two o'clock cardinal saw the skeleton disintegrate and lunged — longsword high, corroded mail rattling, blue fire burning in empty sockets—

The on-kill chain caught it mid-stride. One hundred and five points of force through its midsection. The wight came apart like wet paper. Ash and rust and silence. Vaporized.

The chain didn't break.

---

Two more skeletons in the outer ring — draw, chain, kill. A second wight — chain, kill. Into the middle ring. Four skeletons collapsed inward from their patrol circuit and the blade took them one after another — chain, vaporize, chain, vaporize, chain, kill, chain, kill. The red-black steel hummed with each contact. Ash drifted sideways in the frozen air. The sound was rhythmic: the wet splitting of bone, the *hiss* of vaporization, and under it all, the soft mechanical *shhhing* of the blade continuing its arc from one target to the next without ever stopping.

Five. Ten. Fifteen.

The cardinal wights converged from both flanks — too late. By the time they reached the middle ring, the middle ring was ash. Chain-kill took them both. Seventy-five and a hundred and four through corroded plate. Both crumpled. Neither burned.

Outer ring remnants closed from behind. Four skeletons. They reached him the way moths reach a candle. Chain, vaporize. Chain, vaporize. Chain, kill. Chain, kill.

The middle ring survivors. Two. Both died without slowing the blade.

Twenty kills. Not one sheathe. Not one pause.

---

The inner ring.

Seven skeletons in a shield wall at the threshold. Shields up, swords drawn, formation tight. The tightest defensive formation the command source knew how to build. They watched twenty of their garrison die in fifteen seconds and they held position.

The chain ate through them like acid through linen.

First. Second. Third. Fourth. Fifth. Sixth. Seventh. Each one a single continuation strike — guaranteed crit through the shield, through the rusted mail, through the bone. The shield wall collapsed inward like dominos falling. Bone and rust and ash.

The entrance wight — the heavy one, the bigger armor, the longsword with an edge — brought its weapon up. The chain caught it in the shoulder. One hundred and seven points of force. It folded sideways and crumbled.

Twenty-six kills.

One round.

One breath.

---

Silence.

The frost settled on twenty-six piles of rust and ash and bone fragments. Some were already disappearing — the vaporized ones left nothing but dark smears on the frozen ground. Eight of them. Gone entirely. The others collapsed slowly, metal pieces separating from bone, the last animation leaving them like heat leaving a corpse.

The nodachi completed its arc. Slow. Deliberate. Across the right shoulder, tip skyward, rotating down behind the back.

*Shhhhiiiing.*

*Click.*

---

Jostin's pen was on the page. It hadn't moved in fourteen seconds. There was a line of ink pooling where the nib pressed too hard.

He looked at the empty field. He looked at the twenty-six kill zones. He looked at his prediction — *counterclockwise, start with sentries* — written in his journal, now completely wrong.

He crossed it out with a single line.

Wrote underneath: *Straight line. Through everything. 26. One round.*

He underlined *one round* twice.

---

Brynn's shield dropped two inches during the chain. She caught it. Barely. Her knuckles were white on the grip. Her eyes hadn't blinked. Her mouth was slightly open — the first expression she'd shown that wasn't garrison discipline.

She watched a man walk into a reinforced garrison of twenty-six undead and come out the other side without being touched. Not dodged. Not defended. *Untouched.* The enemies never got a turn. The blade never stopped moving. The ash was still settling.

She pulled the shield back up. Adjusted her grip. Didn't look at him.

Her hands were shaking.

---

### Node 3 — The Relay

---

The structure was identical to the first two — fitted stone, no mortar, Pre-Kingdom precision. The relay stone pulsed at the center. Bruise-colored necromantic light. Bone-ceramic channels.

He drew.

The first strike cracked it — eighty points through enchanted basalt. The channels *screamed*. The stored necromantic energy backlashed outward—

This one hit harder. Reinforced node, more stored energy. The cold wave slammed through the chamber.

Kenji took ten necrotic. Shrugged it off. Jostin staggered into the wall — seventeen necrotic. Coughed. Brynn took fourteen on the shield. Her boots slid back three inches on the stone.

The second strike unmade it. The basalt split into pieces. The bone-ceramic shattered to powder. The bruise-light died.

Living Ground *bloomed*. Two hundred feet in every direction. The ley network exhaled. The dead soil remembered what it was.

---

On the wall beside the doorway — the symbol. But this time it was different.

The circle-and-line was there. Same hand. Same scratch pattern. Recent. But next to it: a **diagonal slash** through the circle. A second marking. Something had been here *after* the first mark was made — and it added to the message.

Jostin saw it. His pen stopped again.

"That's new. The first two had the circle-and-line only. This one has an amendment." He sketched it. "Something came back to this node and *updated* it. Recently. The scratch depth is the same — same tool, same hand. But the slash is newer than the circle. Days, not weeks."

He looked at the ronin.

"Whatever's marking these nodes is revising its notes."

---

### The Blackout

---

And then everything went quiet.

Not the quiet of a dead relay. Not the quiet of a destroyed node. *Everything.*

Living Ground swept south — two hundred feet of restored range — and found **nothing.** No pulse. No hum. No distant necromantic rhythm bleeding through the soil. The entire relay network had gone **silent.** Every node south of here, however many there were, shut down simultaneously.

Total blackout.

Jostin felt it too — the ambient hum that had been under everything since mile five, gone. Like a room where every machine turns off at once.

"That's not a node dying," he said slowly. "That's the whole network going dark. On purpose." He closed the journal. Opened it again. Wrote one word:

*Thinking.*

Then crossed it out and wrote: *Decided.*

---

The south road stretched into grey morning light. Empty. Silent. The frost was thick enough to crack under every step. Three destroyed nodes behind them. An unknown number ahead — but nothing was talking anymore.

Whatever was running this network had just turned everything off at once.

Brynn shifted her shield. Closer than tactical. She hadn't corrected it.

"What now?" Jostin asked. His pen was ready. "The road goes south. The network's dark. Either we're walking into nothing — or we're walking into whatever decided twenty-six wasn't enough."

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter Eleven: *The Voice from the Marsh*

### The Hub

---

South of mile ten the road died. Not corrupted — *abandoned.* The sentries were gone. The relay hum was gone. The frost sat undisturbed on a road no dead thing had walked in hours.

"It pulled everything back," Jostin said. He was writing without looking at the page. "Three nodes down, network dark, and nothing between us and whatever shut it off."

Brynn shifted closer to the ronin's shoulder. Not tactical distance. Bodyguard distance.

They walked two miles in silence.

---

At mile twelve, Living Ground found it. Underground. A structure larger than the three nodes combined — fitted stone, Pre-Kingdom architecture, but this one had *depth.* Multiple chambers. Something alive with necromantic energy at the center, pulsing like a heartbeat.

"That's not a relay," Jostin said. "That's the hub."

The entrance was a stone staircase cut into a hillside. Two wight sentinels flanked it — heavier than the road wights, armored in black plate that still held an edge. They tracked the ronin the moment he appeared.

He drew.

The first wight saw the blade arc and raised its longsword — too late. The iaido strike went through the guard and through the wight behind it. One hundred and twelve points of force. The armor crumpled like foil. Vaporized.

The second wight lunged. The on-kill chain caught it mid-step. Through the neck. Through the spine. It folded and crumbled.

Two kills. One breath.

"I'm going to stop being surprised," Jostin said. "Starting now."

---

### The Bone Architect

---

The hub was one large chamber thirty feet underground. Stone walls. No mortar. The relay stone at the center was three times the size of the node relays — a trunk line, the command node that fed the three capillaries they'd already destroyed.

And standing beside it: a construct.

Something older and stranger than any of the dead they'd faced — neither skeleton nor wight nor revenant. Bone-ceramic and Pre-Kingdom engineering. Humanoid shape, seven feet tall, hands articulated with dozens of joints. It was touching the trunk relay with both hands, fingers splayed across the channels.

It turned when they entered.

"Builders," it said. The voice was dry. Mechanical. Like stone grinding on stone. "You are not builders."

Jostin's bow came up. Brynn's shield snapped forward.

The ronin walked toward it.

"Who do you serve, skeleton guy?"

The construct tilted its head. The articulated fingers lifted from the relay stone.

"I maintain the network. The voice from the deep marsh gives instruction. I execute. Nineteen months. Three capillary nodes. One trunk line. The boundary was to extend north to the river by the solstice."

"The voice from the deep marsh," Jostin repeated. He was writing. "That's the Ashenveil. That's the Lych's territory."

The construct's head tilted the other direction. "I do not know names. I know the voice. The voice commands. I build."

"Take me to your leader."

"I cannot leave the hub. The hub is my function."

---

The ronin looked at Jostin. Jostin looked at the relay — the trunk line still pulsing, still feeding whatever remained of the network south.

"Destroy it," Jostin said. "The construct and the relay. Cut the head off."

The ronin drew.

The construct didn't defend itself. It stood with its articulated hands at its sides and watched the blade come. Two strikes — the first cracked it open, the second scattered the bone-ceramic across the chamber floor. It collapsed like a puppet with the strings cut. No backlash. No scream. Just silence and dust.

The trunk relay was different.

The first strike cracked the basalt. The channels screamed — louder than any node, a sound that vibrated in the teeth and the spine. The stored necromantic energy was *massive.* Nineteen months of accumulated command energy.

The backlash hit like a wall.

Twenty-five necrotic slammed through the ronin. He took it standing. Jostin caught thirty-three — hit the wall, slid down it, coughing blood. Brynn took twenty-one on the shield and her boots scraped back six inches on the stone.

The second strike unmade it. The basalt exploded. The bone-ceramic channels shattered to powder. The bruise-light died.

And Living Ground *bloomed.* Three hundred feet. Four hundred. The suppression that had strangled the ley network for nineteen months collapsed in a single breath. The soil remembered what it was. Root networks fired back to life. The dead zone was dying.

---

"Jostin." Brynn was already moving. She caught the scout before he hit the floor a second time. His face was grey. Blood at the corner of his mouth.

"I'm fine," he said. He wasn't fine. Twenty-eight out of seventy-eight hit points.

"The network's dead," the ronin said. "Permanently. That was the command source."

Jostin coughed. Wiped his mouth. Opened his journal with shaking hands and wrote: *Voice from the deep marsh. 19 months. The Lych.*

---

### Camp — Mile 12

---

They set up above the destroyed hub. Jostin built the fire — smokeless, hidden, garrison training. Brynn cooked. The ronin sat against an oak with the nodachi across his knees.

Long rest rules: can't benefit from more than one in twenty-four hours. Last rest ended around 5 AM Ashmere 27. Next available starting 9 PM.

"We camp twenty hours," Jostin said. "Rest at nine tonight. Move at dawn."

Twenty hours was a long time. But Jostin at twenty-eight HP and Brynn at fifty weren't going anywhere useful.

---

The afternoon passed slow. Jostin slept. Brynn kept watch — shield at her side, eyes on the tree line.

The ronin ate. Stared south. Thought about a voice from the deep marsh that had been building infrastructure for nineteen months without anyone noticing.

---

Evening. The fire burned low. Frost thickening on the grass. Jostin woke, ate, and crawled into his bedroll twenty feet from the fire.

"I'll take second watch if there is one," he said. Then he was gone. Twenty-eight HP will do that.

The ronin looked at Brynn. Brynn looked at the fire.

"If you're scared, I'll share tents with you."

**IP Check — DC 23. Direct flirtation. Eye contact. Firelight.**
**Brynn rolls: 2.**

The last wall fell.

"I'm not scared," she said. Her voice said otherwise.

---

### The Night

---

Kenji stripped down to his smallclothes and sat next to her. Hip to hip.

"It's warmer next to you. Hold me close and keep me warm?"

She opened the blanket without a word. Both arms around him. Full grip. Her chin on top of his head. Her heartbeat hammering against his cheek through thin linen.

"...warm enough?" Two words. Her voice cracked on the second one.

He turned to face her. Pressed his face into the warmth between her breasts.

"So soft... I can stay here forever."

Her arms tightened around his head. Her fingers slid into his dreads at the root. She pulled him closer.

"You have permission to ride me as much as you need tonight, soldier."

She didn't move for three seconds.

Then her hands moved.

---

She used him the way he told her to. Garrison discipline applied to endurance. She was not gentle. She was not quiet.

At one point Jostin coughed from his bedroll. Not a real cough. She didn't stop.

He used his full strength. STR 40. Every position. Every time she bruised he healed it — Diagnostic Touch reading the damage, creation energy erasing it before the marks could form. She felt herself getting stronger instead of weaker. Didn't understand why. Didn't care.

Around 1 AM she was on top again. Face to face. Forehead against his. Tears running down her cheeks.

"Don't stop. Don't ever stop."

He didn't.

Around 3 AM she passed out mid-kiss. Her body gave up what her discipline wouldn't — unconscious, still smiling, still holding him.

Jostin lay in his bedroll with his blanket over his head and contemplated his life choices. The sounds had ranged from alarming to genuinely concerning to quietly devastating. He thought about supply requisition forms. He thought about patrol routes.

He did not think about the fact that at 2 AM the sounds stopped for ten minutes and then started *again.*

*What IS he.*

---

**Lover's Vigor — transmitted.** Creation energy transfer complete.

---

### Morning — Ashmere 28

---

Grey light. Cold. Jostin had a fire going and broth in the pot. His eyes were bloodshot. His expression was aggressively neutral.

"Morning. Broth's ready. We should move by seven."

A pause. He glanced at the blanket situation. Looked away.

"...I'll be over here."

---

Brynn pulled on her armor and paused. The breastplate went up and over her head — one-handed. The buckles closed faster. The shield—

She picked it up. Stared at it. Forty pounds of riveted steel felt like a dinner plate.

"Brynn." Jostin was watching.

"What."

"Your eyes."

"What about them."

"They're gold."

She touched her face. "I'm fine." The tone said *do not pursue this.*

---

### The March North

---

"Alright guys, let's continue to the objective."

The road north. Heading back toward Thornkeep. The relay network was dead — the road felt *alive* for the first time in months. Grass pushing through frost. Lichen on barren stones. The corruption pulling back like a tide.

But there were stragglers. Masterless undead — skeletons and wights left on patrol when the network died. Wandering. Confused. Some standing in the road staring at nothing.

The ronin walked point but didn't draw. He nodded at Brynn and Jostin.

*Your kills.*

---

Mile 11. Four skeletons in a cluster. Jostin took three — clean, professional. Brynn hit the fourth with her shield.

The skeleton *exploded.* Bones scattered across fifteen feet.

"...what," Brynn said.

"Brynn, what the hell was that?"

"I don't *know.*"

---

Mile 10. Two wights at the destroyed Node 3 site. Brynn walked straight at them. Shield bash — the first wight flew ten feet and hit a tree. She was on it before it stood. Longsword through the ribcage, twist, pull. The second clawed her back — 4 damage. She barely felt it. Spun, shield-checked it to the ground, stamped on its skull.

Eight seconds.

Jostin looked at the ronin. The ronin was leaning against a tree. Arms crossed.

"I feel..." She rolled her sword wrist. The blade spun — a move she'd never had the wrist speed for. "I feel *good.*"

---

Mile 9. Six skeletons. Jostin took three. Brynn took three — and cleaved the last one shoulder to hip with one hand.

She looked at the two halves. She looked at her arm.

"Jostin."

"Yep."

"Don't tell the commander about this."

"About what."

"*Any* of this."

"Telling her about what, Brynn? I slept through everything. My eyes are bad. I don't know what color gold is."

She almost smiled. The first real expression all morning. It died fast — but it was there.

---

Mile 8. Mid-morning. The frost burning off. The treeline greening.

Brynn walked beside the ronin. Shield on her back. Her amber-gold eyes kept flicking to him — quick glances she thought he didn't catch.

He caught all of them.

Four miles to Thornkeep.

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter Twelve: *The Formation*

### The Turn

---

Mile eight. Four miles from Thornkeep. The road home.

Jostin had the journal open. Already writing the debrief. Already formatting the report for Bracken — three nodes, one hub, one construct, one trunk relay. The whole network dead. Clean win. Time to go home.

"We're not going back."

Jostin's pen stopped.

"Sir?"

"The network's dead. The road's clear. Whatever was running this operation is south. I want to find it."

Jostin looked at the cleared road behind them. Looked at the road ahead — south, into territory they hadn't scouted. Looked at Brynn. Brynn looked at the ronin.

"I want to find whatever that Bone Architect was talking to. The voice from the marsh. It's been building for nineteen months. I just broke its toy. It knows we're here. If I walk back to Thornkeep, it rebuilds. If I walk south—"

"You find it before it has time to think." Jostin closed the journal. "That's either brilliant or suicidal."

"Those have been the same thing all week."

Brynn shifted the shield to her other hand. "Food in the satchel if you want it, sir."

---

### The Cleared Road

---

Miles eight through twelve were a graveyard of their own making. Every node they'd destroyed was a scar in the earth — cracked stone, shattered basalt, the bruise-light dead. But the land between was *waking up.* Grass pushing through frost. Lichen on barren stones. A bird at mile nine — the first living sound any of them had heard south of the mist line.

"Living Ground's at full range," the ronin said. "Two hundred feet. Everything's clean."

Brynn took the stragglers. Four masterless skeletons at mile ten — standing in the road where Node 3 used to be, staring at nothing. She walked through them like a plow through wheat. Shield, sword, shield, stomp. The whole cluster down before the second one finished falling.

Jostin took two more at mile eleven. Clean arrows. Professional.

The ronin didn't draw.

---

### Mile Twelve — The Hub

---

They passed the destroyed hub without stopping. The hillside entrance gaped open — dark, silent, the stone staircase going down to nothing. The Bone Architect's chamber was rubble and dust. The trunk relay was powder.

"Nineteen months," Jostin said quietly. "Whatever that voice was, it spent nineteen months building this. And we killed it in a day."

"Which means it's angry."

"Or impressed."

"Let's hope angry. Angry makes mistakes."

---

### New Territory — Miles 13-15

---

South of mile twelve the world changed.

The corruption here was *active* — no longer the passive drain of the relay network. Living Ground read something different. Root networks in the soil, neither natural growth nor ley lines. Necromantic infrastructure woven through the marsh earth. A sensory web. The same kind of system that had detected living intrusion at the Ashenveil border months ago.

"The ground's alive," the ronin said. "Wrong kind of alive."

Jostin crouched. Touched the frost. "The temperature dropped three degrees in the last hundred yards. And the mist—"

The mist was back. Not the thin fog of the relay zone. This was *marsh mist* — thick, cold, knee-high, rolling south from somewhere they couldn't see.

Living Ground contracted. Two hundred feet to a hundred and fifty. To a hundred.

"We're being watched," the ronin said. "The root network knows we're here."

"How long?"

"Since we crossed mile thirteen."

Brynn's shield came up. She didn't ask questions. She didn't need to.

---

Mile fourteen. Six skeleton sentries in the road. Different from the relay guards — heavier armor, better formation. These weren't leftovers. These were *fresh.*

"New stock," Jostin said. "Not from the network. Deployed after the blackout."

Brynn took four. Jostin took two.

Mile fourteen and a half. The road dipped into a shallow valley. Marsh water on both sides — stagnant, black, the surface still. The mist thickened to waist-height. Living Ground was at eighty feet and shrinking.

"Sir." Brynn's voice was quiet. "My shield's vibrating."

"That's the root network. It's under us."

"Under us *how far?*"

"Everywhere."

---

### The Clone — Mile 15.5

---

The ronin stopped walking.

"Hold here."

Jostin and Brynn stopped. The road stretched south into grey nothing. The mist was chest-high. Living Ground at sixty feet — and at the edge of perception, something massive.

Not one thing. Many things. Standing in formation. A wall of dead things across the road, packed tight, shields up. And behind them — three signatures that burned colder than anything the relay network had produced. And one more. One that wasn't dead.

"There's a formation ahead. Forty-plus. Three big ones behind them. And something alive."

Jostin's pen stopped. "Alive?"

"Human-sized. Living signature. Thirty yards west of the formation. Just... standing there."

"That's not undead behavior."

"No. It isn't."

---

Smoke bomb. The cloud rolled out low — grey-white, hugging the mist. Invisibility. Clone.

The clone materialized in the smoke's wake. Same gear, same stance, same nodachi across the back. It fell into step between Jostin and Brynn.

The real Kenji was already gone. Wind Step to a dead oak sixty yards west. Elevated position. Full sensory suite — God Sight, Living Ground, Bond-Form Sight. Invisible. Silent. Watching.

Jostin glanced at the clone. His pen moved. He wrote something small in the margin of his journal and kept walking.

He'd noticed. He didn't say a word.

---

### The Wall

---

The formation emerged from the mist like a nightmare given geometry.

Forty-two skeletons in a shield wall. Not the ragged sentries of the relay zone — these were *garrison quality.* Interlocking shields, swords drawn, formation tight enough to stop a cavalry charge. Three ranks deep. They filled the road from ditch to ditch.

Behind them: three revenants. Not wights — *revenants.* Armored in black plate that still held its polish. Blue fire in the eye sockets burned steady and bright. Each one stood a head taller than the skeletons. Each one radiated cold that made the mist curl away from their feet.

And on the west flank, thirty yards from the formation, partially screened by dead marsh birch — the living signature. Human-sized. Alive. Holding still.

The clone walked point. Jostin behind, journal out, writing without looking. Brynn shield-right, amber-gold eyes locked on the wall ahead.

The formation didn't move. Forty-two skulls tracked the approaching party. Forty-two swords stayed drawn. The revenants watched with the patience of things that had been dead long enough to stop hurrying.

The root network pulsed underfoot. A signal sent south. Deep into the marsh.

*They know.*

---

From the dead oak, invisible, Kenji watched. The living signature on the west flank hadn't moved. Hadn't reacted to the party's approach. Just stood there — same stature, same living read, watching the formation from the tree line the same way Kenji was watching from above.

Thirty yards from the real Kenji's tree. Close enough that Living Ground read details: heartbeat steady, breathing slow, no armor signature, no weapon drawn. Whoever it was, they weren't here to fight.

They were here to observe.

Kenji filed the rhythm — slow breath, steady pulse, no hunger-shake in the legs. *Field posture,* not camp posture. Whatever report that body owed, it would travel on roots later; he did not know yet that the same heartbeat would stand at mile 16.5 in a Coalition tabard with a collar-leash, but Living Ground had already learned the gait.

The clone kept walking. Fifty yards from the wall. Forty. Thirty.

The mist curled around Brynn's boots. Jostin's pen scratched. The revenants' blue fire reflected off forty-two rusted shields.

Twenty yards.

The formation held.

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter Thirteen: *The Shield Wall*

### The Draw

---

Twenty yards.

The clone stopped walking. Jostin's pen stopped scratching. Brynn's shield came up another inch.

Forty-two skulls stared. Forty-two swords held steady. The revenants behind the line burned blue and patient.

From the dead oak sixty yards west, invisible, Kenji dropped.

Wind Step. The world compressed to a single line — oak to rear rank center — and then he was *there*, behind the wall, behind the revenants, standing in the space between the third rank and the command layer where no enemy expected a living thing to exist.

Invisibility shattered on arrival. Purple dreads caught the mist-light. The nodachi was still sheathed across his back.

One heartbeat of silence. Every skull in the rear rank rotated.

Iaido.

The draw came from the shoulder — a single upward arc that caught the first skeleton at the collarbone and split it crown to pelvis. Guaranteed critical. The nodachi's void edge carved through bone and binding both, and the skeleton didn't fall so much as *separate*, the two halves drifting apart like pages of a book dropped in wind. Purple-black mist where the marrow should have been.

The blade didn't stop.

On-Kill Continuation. The nodachi swept left into the next skeleton before the first one's shield hit the ground. Another clean split. Another kill. The chain had started.

---

### The Chain

---

Six rounds. That was all it took.

The rear rank died in the first ten seconds — Kenji's opening iaido draw chained through skeleton after skeleton, each kill earning the next swing, the nodachi a continuous arc of dark steel and void energy that turned the back line into a corridor of falling bones. The formation tried to adjust. Shields rotated inward. The middle rank compressed to fill the gap.

It didn't matter.

Kenji moved through them the way water moves through a dam crack — finding the seam, widening it, pouring through. Two base attacks per round. Every kill chained into a free swing. The nodachi's 6d12 was grotesque overkill against skeleton-grade HP, which meant almost every hit was a kill, and every kill was another attack.

Round two. The revenants turned. Black plate, blue fire, coordination that suggested memory rather than instinct. They were the real threat — CR 5 each, armored, multi-attack, necrotic riders on every swing.

Kenji prioritized them.

The first revenant took a critical to the shoulder that carved through the pauldron and into the ribcage beneath. It staggered but didn't drop — 150 hit points of binding-grade undead don't die to one swing. The second attack finished it. The blue fire in its eyes guttered, flared, and went out. It fell in two pieces. The void edge had hit something fundamental in the binding, and the revenant's armor *dissolved* — vaporized, reduced to black mist that the wind took south.

The skeletons kept pressing. Six could reach him per round — sword strikes that pinged off AC 19 like hail off a temple roof. The ones that missed earned counters. Two free reaction strikes per round, each one powerful enough to split a skeleton in half.

Round three. Round four. The second revenant went down — another vaporization on a critical hit, the 25% chance landing twice in one fight. The third revenant lasted longer, landing a necrotic-laced strike that Kenji's regeneration erased before the bruise finished forming. 333 HP per round. Full regeneration. The revenant could have hit him all day and never made progress.

It didn't get all day. It got half a round.

Round five. The skeleton count was in single digits. The formation had stopped being a formation somewhere around round three — just individual skeletons swinging at a target that moved too fast and hit too hard. Kenji cut through the last cluster near the road's east ditch, the nodachi splitting two with a single horizontal sweep.

Round six. The last skeleton fell.

Forty-five kills. Forty-five out of forty-five. Two vaporized. Zero damage sustained that outlasted his regeneration. Six rounds from first draw to final sheathe.

The road was clear. Bone fragments and rusted shields littered the packed dirt from ditch to ditch. The mist curled through the gaps where a formation had been.

---

### The Pursuit

---

From the road's north edge, the clone had already moved. While Kenji was dismantling the wall from behind, the robed figure on the west flank — the living signature, the observer — had broken and run south the moment the iaido draw came out. Smart enough to know what it was seeing. Smart enough not to wait for the skeletons to finish dying.

Kenji sheathed the nodachi. Full sheathe — the cord tied, the weapon seated across his back, iaido stance reset. He wiped bone dust off the back of his hand and looked south.

"Their leader is still up ahead. Let's see where it ran off to."

The clone took point with Jostin and Brynn, heading south at a jog. Nothing left to fight — every skeleton that had stood in that formation was bone fragments on the road behind them. The only thing still moving south was the observer.

Kenji walked. Unhurried. Hand resting on the nodachi's hilt at his shoulder. The mist was thicker past mile 16, chest-high, and the root network under the road had changed character — the thin sensory tendrils giving way to thick trunks, each one wider than a man's leg, converging south like the spokes of a wheel toward something Kenji couldn't see yet.

---

### Mile 16.5 — The Junction

---

The roots converged in a clearing.

Six trunks — massive, each thicker than the road itself — met at a central point where the packed dirt gave way to a lattice of exposed root material. Necrotic nodules dimpled the surfaces, pulsing faint green in sequence. South. Always south. The rhythm was slower than the relay network had been. Deeper. This wasn't communication. This was *circulation.*

The robed figure stood at the junction's center.

The clone arrived first, closing to thirty feet. The figure turned fully, and Living Ground read the details before conscious observation caught up: human, male, gaunt but not undead-gaunt — *starved*. Sunken eyes with burst capillaries. A leather collar sat tight against his throat, and from it, a single root tendril descended into the ground at his feet like a leash. His robes were Coalition-issue. A courier's tabard, mud-caked, the rank badge torn off but the thread-holes still visible.

He held the relay stone out at arm's length. Not as a weapon. As an offering. Or a report.

Living Ground confirmed what the pursuit had already implied: same human frame as the west-flank watcher at mile 15.5 — the runner had simply arrived here first, ahead of the party, to stand where the circulation trunks wanted a mouth.

"She'll want to know how a dead man's puppet fights like *that*."

His voice cracked. Dry. Days without real water. His eyes flicked to the clone's nodachi, then back to its face.

"You're not him. The real one's behind me. I can feel the roots *screaming* where he walked."

The collar pulsed once. His jaw tightened — involuntary, like a flinch from inside.

"I have... seven words left before she pulls me back."

He swallowed.

"The knight is coming. Don't be here."

The relay stone went dark. The root at his collar *yanked* — not metaphorically — his body jerked backward two feet, boots dragging furrows in the dirt, and then he was sliding south along the root channel — pulled fast, pulled hard — disappearing into the mist between the dead trunks.

Silence. The junction pulsed once more — green, south — and went still.

---

### The Clearing After

---

Jostin and Brynn were forty yards back. Jostin had his shortbow half-drawn, arrow nocked but not aimed. Brynn had her shield up, watching the root lines on either side of the road.

Real Kenji walked up. Unhurried. The mist curled around him at knee height. The clone turned and looked back at him. Waiting.

The junction was empty. The root trunks still converged. The nodules had gone dark — no pulse, no green, no signal. Whatever the courier had been reporting to, it had received the message and gone quiet.

Kenji lifted two fingers — dismiss. The clone unraveled into gray smoke that thinned against Jostin's veil discipline without fight; no second charge spent, only the projection ended before anything else on the road could treat it as a second Kenji worth chasing.

Jostin lowered the bow. "Coalition courier tabard. Rank badge stripped. He's been out here... weeks, maybe. The collar—" He stopped. Wrote something in the journal margin. "The collar was a root leash. She's using live conscripts as field observers."

Brynn said nothing. She was staring south, where the courier had disappeared. Her amber-gold eyes caught the last green pulse before it died.

"'The knight is coming,'" Jostin repeated. He looked at Kenji. "Corwyn?"

The mist pressed in. The junction was quiet. The road south vanished into it after twenty yards.

---

## Fraying Empire — Chapter 14: *Oathbreaker*

**Session span:** Ashmere 28 late afternoon through Ashmere 29 dawn (Day 250–251).  
**Corridor:** South road / east verge — miles ~16.5–19.5, Pallid March mist.

---

### Cold Signals

---

The junction stayed dark for three minutes after the courier disappeared south. Three minutes of root trunks pulsing nothing, mist curling through dead wood, and three people standing in a clearing that had just swallowed a man on a leash.

Jostin broke the silence first. Not with words — with his journal. Pen moving in tight, controlled strokes. Cataloguing. Filing. The scout's version of breathing exercises.

Brynn watched south. Shield up. Amber-gold eyes scanning the tree line where the courier had slid into the mist like something reeled in on a wire.

The ronin looked at his people, then looked at the road, and made the calculation that commanders make when the enemy knows they're coming and the only advantage left is geometry.

He split the party.

Not a retreat split — a *tactical* split. Jostin and Brynn would leave first, moving east off the crown onto the verge, then north along the birch line toward the waypoint he'd chalked at mile sixteen-point-nine in camp margin code. Their job was signal and shelter: Brynn's ring-fire when she had line of sight to the junction, Jostin's smaller burns answering on a stagger so the mist read living discipline, not panic. If a death knight came up the road — and the courier had said a death knight was coming up the road — he would follow the wheel ruts, the packed center, the path that read like an army's spine. He would not look east into birch scrub for a scout and a shield line hiding behind watch-fires.

Jostin closed the journal. One nod. Professional.

Brynn's eyes found the ronin's face — held there for a beat longer than discipline required — and then she turned east. Shield leading. Boots quiet on the frost.

They disappeared into the birch line in under a minute. Good movement. Clean lines.

The ronin stayed on the crown.

---

Smoke bomb. The cloud rolled low — grey-white, mist-colored, invisible against the ambient fog. Invisibility. Clone.

Kenji-two materialized in the smoke's wake. Same mask, same nodachi across the back, same unhurried walk. It started south down the crown — a second silhouette moving along the packed center where Corwyn's approach would register first. A decoy and a tripwire in one body.

The real Kenji followed at fifty yards, alternating between the crown and the east verge. Split-brief fires stacked as they moved: Brynn's waypoint to the northeast, Kenji's answer-flame at the junction behind, a second south-column burn when the clone pushed past mile seventeen-point-five. At the fence post there, Kenji pressed milepost chalk into the wood — a mark for Jostin's hand if the mist tried to steal bearings.

The root network under the road was quiet. Not dead — *quiet*. The circulation trunks still pulsed at depths Living Ground could barely read. Whatever the courier had reported, the audience had received it. The audience was thinking.

Mile seventeen. Seventeen-point-five. The clone walked point. The mist thickened. Living Ground contracted to a hundred feet, then eighty.

Then Brynn's fire didn't read clean from the south position.

Not gone — *wrong*. Shifted east by thirty yards, the ring pattern disrupted, the stagger broken. Either she had moved or something had moved her perception of where the signal should go.

Kenji burned Wind Step. Three charges — one to close north on her vector, one to correct the approach angle when the birch line shifted underfoot, one to light the Brynn-slot ring east of the crown where the watch-fire pattern said *I am here and I am not lost.*

He found them exactly where they should have been. Jostin crouched behind a fallen birch, arrow nocked, scanning south through the mist. Brynn shield-right, amber-gold eyes tracking movement that turned out to be wind through dead branches.

The fire shift had been wind. Just wind.

But the charges were spent. Wind Step 5/5 → 0/5. The road would have to be walked from here on legs that could not skip across treetops.

---

### Ridge Thread

---
